# Changelog

Detailed changelog for Perry. See CLAUDE.md for concise summaries.

## v0.5.410 — Closes #320: filed against v0.5.405 reporting `Undefined symbols for architecture arm64: _js_readable_stream_new, _js_readable_stream_controller_close, _js_readable_stream_controller_enqueue, _js_readable_stream_controller_error` at the link step when compiling Effect's `Stream` module after the v0.5.403 / v0.5.405 codegen wins (#309 / #310). The four FFI symbols and the surrounding ReadableStream / WritableStream / TransformStream / reader / writer / `pipeTo` / `pipeThrough` surface are all already implemented in `crates/perry-stdlib/src/streams.rs` (38 `#[no_mangle]` extern "C" entries, 1300+ lines; registered via `pub mod streams; pub use streams::*;` at `crates/perry-stdlib/src/lib.rs:80,82`) — landed in #237/#301 (PR #301 merged 2026-04-29 17:44 UTC, ~9h before #320 was filed and three on-main commits ahead of the v0.5.405 cut available at the time of writing; the issue reporter likely missed that #237 had just merged during the same #309/#310 sweep). The codegen side at `crates/perry-codegen/src/lower_call.rs:3469-3584` already wires all 14 dispatch sites for `js_readable_stream_*` (`get_reader`, `cancel`, `tee`, `pipe_to`, `pipe_through`, `locked`, `controller_enqueue`, `controller_close`, `controller_error`, `controller_desired_size`) and `crates/perry-codegen/src/runtime_decls.rs:966-993` declares all 12 LLVM externs. Verified the issue's literal minimal repro on `main` HEAD: `new ReadableStream({ start(controller) { controller.enqueue("hello"); controller.close(); } }); console.log(stream)` compiles cleanly, links cleanly, runs to exit 0 — no `Undefined symbols` error. The cosmetic `console.log(stream)` rendering still shows `1` (raw registry-id-as-f64 handle) instead of Node's `ReadableStream { locked: false, state: 'readable', supportsBYOB: false }` — but this is a generic console-formatter dispatch limitation across all handle-based registries (same `id as f64` pattern used by `BLOB_REGISTRY`, `FETCH_RESPONSES`, `READERS`, `WRITERS`, `TRANSFORM_STREAMS`), not a stream implementation gap. Stream handles cast to f64 are bit-indistinguishable from numeric values, so console.log can't dispatch on them without either NaN-boxing every handle as POINTER_TAG (breaks all existing `as usize` extraction sites in `lower_call.rs`) or threading static-type info through console.log lowering (multi-day codegen change). Out of scope for #320, which documents the link error specifically — the link error is gone. **All four "adjacent gaps" listed in #320's body are also already covered by #237/#301**: `WritableStream` + writer surface, `TransformStream`, `ReadableStreamDefaultReader` via `js_readable_stream_get_reader` + `js_reader_*` (read / cancel / release_lock / closed_promise), `ReadableStreamDefaultController` exposed implicitly as the stream handle itself per the inline comment at `streams.rs:411` ("the new stream's controller is the stream handle itself"), `pipeTo` at `streams.rs:812`, `pipeThrough` at `streams.rs:891`, `Response.body` wired via `alloc_readable_from_bytes` at `streams.rs:435` (called from the fetch path's response wrapper). New regression test `test-files/test_issue_320_readable_stream.ts` pins the issue's exact code shape (string-chunk `controller.enqueue("hello")` — distinct from the existing #237 tests which all use `Uint8Array` chunks: `_streams_blob` exercises `blob.stream()` over byte buffers, `_streams_pipe` exercises `pipeTo` / `pipeThrough` / `tee` chains, `_streams_user_source` exercises `controller.enqueue(new Uint8Array([...]))` not strings) — matches `node --experimental-strip-types` byte-for-byte for `r1/r2/r3.{done,value}`. **Verification**: cargo build --release -p perry-runtime -p perry-stdlib -p perry clean; gap tests 27/28 = baseline (lone fail is the pre-existing `console_methods` ci-env quirk); all 3 existing #237 stream regression tests still match Node byte-for-byte (no regression from the #320 pin); new `test_issue_320_readable_stream.ts` matches Node byte-for-byte on first run. Companion follow-up under umbrella #321 (Effect framework end-to-end compat) — unblocks any Effect module that imported `Stream`, plus general Node 18+ code touching `fetch().body` or `node:stream/web`.

## v0.5.403 — Closes #309: `perry compile` of a 4-line program importing the `effect` package OOM'd at **34 GB RSS / 249 GB peak virtual** before being SIGKILL'd ~7 minutes in, during the `Generating code...` phase. **Root cause**: an inheritance-chain cycle in `compile_module`'s `class_table`. Effect declares same-named classes across modules — e.g. `class Base extends Class<any>` inside Data.ts's `TaggedClass` IIFE, plus `class Class<A,E,R> extends Base<A,E,R>` in Effectable.ts. When the cross-module-import resolver pulls every exported class into Data.ts's `imported_class_stubs` (the v0.5.362 #240 augmentation fires whenever a module references an unresolved type name — the kind Effect generates by the dozen via `arguments`-based `dual()` helpers and bare `A`/`B`/`E1`/`R1` generics), the stub for `Class` carries `parent_name = "Base"` from Effectable's source. In Data.ts's importing namespace, that `"Base"` resolves to Data.ts's OWN local `Base` (different class, same name), whose `extends_name = "Class"` resolves to the imported stub: ⟶ `Base → Class → Base → Class → …` cycle. Every chain-walking site in codegen (and there are ~30 of them: `apply_field_initializers_recursive`, `class_field_global_index`, `static_type_of`'s `PropertyGet` arm, the `class_keys_init_data` parent walk, `receiver_class_name`, etc.) assumed acyclic inheritance. Specifically `apply_field_initializers_recursive` accumulated visited names into `chain: Vec<String>` without bound — that's where the 34 GB RSS came from: a `String` for every cycle iteration on every field-init application call, in a tight `while let Some(c) = cur` loop. Other chain walkers that count rather than accumulate would CPU-hang at constant memory but make zero progress. **Fix is one centralized cycle break in `compile_module`** at `crates/perry-codegen/src/codegen.rs:435+` — runs ONCE after `imported_class_stubs` are built but BEFORE they're added to `class_table`. For each stub, walk the (local ∪ stub) parent chain via DFS in the union name space (preferring local hir.classes over stubs, matching the downstream `class_table.entry().or_insert()` semantics), tracking visited names in a HashSet and capping depth at 64. If the walk revisits a name OR exceeds the cap, the stub is part of a cycle: drop its `extends_name` to `None`, breaking the cycle at the imported side (the local class is left untouched since we can't mutate `hir.classes`). Subsequent chain walks in `apply_field_initializers_recursive`, `class_field_global_index`, `static_type_of`, etc. now operate on a guaranteed-acyclic graph. The fundamental name-collision issue (Data.ts's local `Base` and Effectable.ts's `Base` are different classes despite sharing a name) is left unfixed — a proper resolution requires module-prefixing class names in HIR (e.g. `Base$node_modules_effect_src_Data_ts$TaggedClass` instead of bare `Base`), which is a multi-day refactor with breaking implications for the entire dispatch / `instanceof` / class-id machinery; the cycle break here is purely defensive and lets compilation proceed even when name collisions occur. **Verified end-to-end** on the issue's exact Effect 3.21.2 repro: `cd /Users/amlug/projects/effect-oom-test && /usr/bin/time -l perry compile test_direct.ts -o /tmp/effect-out` — pre-fix 430s wall / 34 GB RSS / SIGKILL exit 137; post-fix **2.72s wall / 133 MB max RSS / 123 MB peak memory footprint** — a **256× memory reduction and 158× faster wall time**. All 152 modules compile cleanly to .o files. The link step then fails with separate `ld: symbol(s) not found` errors for unresolved cross-module method symbols (e.g. `_perry_method_node_modules_effect_src_internal_redBlackTree_iterator_ts__RedBlackTreeIterator__next`) — these are pre-existing dispatch gaps for specific Effect patterns (likely the v0.5.362 polymorphic-receiver augmentation pulling in classes whose method bodies don't get emitted), tracked separately as the natural follow-up to "perry compile *and links* an Effect app". The OOM that #309 documented is fully fixed; the link-time gaps are next. **Verified no regression**: gap tests 27/28 = baseline (lone failure remains the documented `console_methods` ci-env quirk); inheritance-chain regression smoke (3-level Animal/Dog/Puppy with super-method calls) compiles + runs and produces expected output; existing #212 (class method capture) / #240 (interface dispatch) / #261 (class field closure init) regression tests all match `node --experimental-strip-types` byte-for-byte. The cycle break runs in O(stubs × chain-depth) which is bounded (depth-cap 64 × 45-ish stubs per module × 152 modules = ~440k HashSet inserts max, fractional-second cost) — invisible on every measured workload.

## v0.5.402 — Closes #311: `for...of` on a Map/Set held as a property of a plain object literal OR a class instance silently iterated zero times. v0.5.388's #302 fix widened the for-of iterable resolver from `Ident`-only to also handle `Member { obj: This, prop }` (class-field-via-`this`), but `obj.<prop>` (where `obj` is a regular local) and `instance.<field>` (where `instance` is `new C()` — the variant the issue reporter flagged on top of the original repro) both still fell through to `_ => None`. Loop then read `.length` on a raw Map handle (returns 0) and produced no iterations. Same root cause as #302, two more missing arms. **Fix** in both for-of lowering sites (`crates/perry-hir/src/lower.rs:5417` and `crates/perry-hir/src/lower_decl.rs:3676`): widen the `Member` arm so when `m.obj` is anything other than `This`, infer the receiver's type via `crate::lower_types::infer_type_from_expr` and dispatch on the result — `Type::Object(ot)` looks the property up via `ot.properties.get(prop).map(|pi| pi.ty.clone())` (covers `const obj = { m }; for-of obj.m`); `Type::Named(cls)` consults the same `class_field_types` registry the `this.<field>` arm uses (covers `const ex = new Example(); for-of ex.m` where `Example`'s `m: Map<K, V>` is a declared class field — already populated by the v0.5.388 early-pass `register_class_field_types`). New regression test `test-files/test_issue_311_object_property_for_of.ts` (9 cases — Map / Set / Array shorthand `{ m }`, KeyValue `{ items: m2 }`, nested wrapper with renamed property, #302 local-Map regression guard, plus class-instance Map / Set / Array fields) matches `node --experimental-strip-types` byte-for-byte. Verified: cargo build --release clean; gap tests 27/28 = baseline (lone failure remains the documented `console_methods` ci-env quirk); existing #302 test still matches Node byte-for-byte.

## v0.5.401 — HarmonyOS Phase 2 v1.5: full widget set in `perry-codegen-arkts`. Builds on v0.5.399 (PR #308 — Phase 2 v1 with just `Text` support). Adds **VStack / HStack / Button / TextField / Toggle / Slider / Spacer / Divider** widget arms, **recursive child-array walking** for stack containers, **LocalGet escape** so `const t = Text("hi"); App({body: t})` follows the binding back to its init, and **nested layout support** (VStack of HStacks of Text+Spacer+Text validated end-to-end). 11 new test cases in `crates/perry-codegen-arkts/src/lib.rs::tests` cover every widget arm + nesting + LocalGet (15/15 unit tests pass). Each widget is one match arm in `emit_widget` + one ArkUI shape line — same template the next 20+ widgets will follow. **Widget mappings**: `VStack(spacing?, [...])` → `Column({space: <n>})`, `HStack` → `Row`, `Button("label", onPress)` → `Button('label')`, `TextField(placeholder, onChange)` → `TextInput({placeholder: '...'})`, `Toggle(label, onChange)` → `Row { Text + Toggle({type: ToggleType.Switch}) }` (label rendered as sibling Text since ArkUI's Toggle has no label param), `Slider(min, max, onChange)` → `Slider({min, max, value: min, step: 1, style: SliderStyle.OutSet})`, `Spacer()` → `Blank()`, `Divider()` → `Divider()`. **Closures dropped silently**: Button's onPress, TextField's onChange, etc. — widgets render but don't fire Perry TS callbacks yet. The architectural fit is a NAPI bridge between ArkUI's `@State`/`@Link` and Perry's runtime `State<T>` — deferred to Phase 2 v2 since it requires bidirectional handle marshaling that's a real design exercise. **`fmt_num` helper**: emits whole-number floats without decimals (`8` not `8.0`) to match ArkUI's idiomatic style. **`resolve` helper + `collect_const_bindings`**: top-level `Stmt::Let { id, init: Some(expr), mutable: false }` builds a `HashMap<LocalId, Expr>` keyed by the immutable LocalId; `emit_widget` consults this on every recursive call so any widget-typed `LocalGet` resolves transparently. Doesn't follow nested-block lets or mutable bindings — those need a wider analysis pass and aren't blocking the common patterns. **Verified**: `cargo test --release -p perry-codegen-arkts` 15/15; multi-widget compile of `App({body: VStack(16, [Text(...), Divider(), HStack([Text, Spacer, Text]), Button(...), TextField(...), Toggle(...), Slider(...)])})` produces 1123-byte ArkUI Index.ets with all expected widget arms emitted at correct indentation. End-to-end smoke on DevEco emulator pending user re-run; the unit tests + structural emission validation are the proof points for this PR. Bumped above origin's parallel-track v0.5.400 (#303 — Win7 compat) per the merge-collision precedent.

## v0.5.400 — Closes #303: opt-in Win7 / Win8 / 8.1 compatibility for compiled executables via new `--min-windows-version=7|8|10` CLI flag (default `10`). Two coordinated changes — (1) **PE subsystem flag**: `crates/perry/src/commands/compile/library_search.rs::windows_pe_subsystem_flag` now appends `,5.1` (Win7) or `,6.02` (Win8) to `/SUBSYSTEM:` when `--min-windows-version` is set. Default emits no suffix (linker default = Win10+). Threaded through `CompilationContext` from `CompileArgs::min_windows_version`. Invalid values fail at parse time, not silently. (2) **Lazy DPI retrofit**: new `crates/perry-ui-windows/src/dpi_compat.rs` (211 LOC) replaces the previously-static imports of `SetProcessDpiAwarenessContext` (Win10 1607+) and `GetDpiForSystem` (Win10 1607+) with `LoadLibraryA + GetProcAddress` lookups, falling through Win10 → Win8.1 (`SetProcessDpiAwareness`) → Vista (`SetProcessDPIAware`) tiers for DPI awareness, and Win10 (`GetDpiForSystem`) → Win2000 (`GetDC + GetDeviceCaps(LOGPIXELSY)`) for system-DPI lookup. Cached in `AtomicPtr` + `AtomicU8` so the lookup runs once per process. The retrofit is unconditional (active on default builds too) — robustifies against stripped-down Windows installs at no measurable cost. Pre-fix the static imports caused the Win7 loader to refuse the binary before `main()` ran with "entry point SetProcessDpiAwarenessContext could not be located in user32.dll". **What works on Win7 SP1**: every standard widget (`Button`, `TextField`, `SecureField`, `Toggle`, `Slider`, `Picker`, `ProgressView`, `Canvas`, `Image`, `Form`, `LazyVStack`), all layout containers, file/folder dialogs, clipboard, audio (WASAPI is Vista+), menus, toolbars, multi-window, and the full perry-runtime + perry-stdlib surface. **What degrades silently on Win7**: per-monitor DPI re-scaling (Win10+), dark titlebar (Win10 1809+), rounded window corners (Win11+), Mica/Acrylic backdrop (Win11+) — call returns error, perry swallows it, app keeps running. **What's outright impossible on Win7**: anything that pulls in `perry/jsruntime` (V8 / deno_core embeds Win10+ unconditionally) — TS programs that import `.js` modules from `node_modules` auto-enable jsruntime and won't load. New docs page `docs/src/platforms/windows-7.md` (123 LOC) covers TL;DR, accepted values, what works/degrades/is impossible, lazy DPI internals, validation steps, caveats; wired into `docs/src/SUMMARY.md` under Platforms; cross-referenced from `docs/src/platforms/windows.md`. **Validated** on Win11 PowerShell against `llvm-objdump -p`: `ui-win7.exe` declares PE subsystem version 5.01 (Major=5, Minor=1, Subsystem=Windows GUI), `hello-win7.exe` declares 5.01 CUI, `ui-default.exe` declares 6.00 GUI, `hello-default.exe` declares 6.00 CUI. `SetProcessDpiAwarenessContext` and `GetDpiForSystem` absent from import tables of all 4 builds (the lazy retrofit is universal). Lazy-loader stubs `LoadLibraryA + GetProcAddress + SetProcessDPIAware (Vista+) + GetDeviceCaps` all present in both UI builds. All 4 binaries run cleanly on Win11; UI windows open with the expected title and exit cleanly. Win7 VM step deliberately skipped — static PE evidence is sufficient per the doc's own framing. Also fixes a pre-existing unresolved-conflict-markers bug on `main`'s CLAUDE.md from the v0.5.399 HarmonyOS PR #308 merge (both at the Current Version line and changelog) — picked up as a side effect of editing the same regions.

## v0.5.399 — HarmonyOS Phase 2 v1: TS→ArkUI emission via new `perry-codegen-arkts` crate. Closes the loop on Phase 1 (PRs #246-#253 + #290): users can now write `App({body: Text("hi")})` in TypeScript and Perry compiles it to a real ArkUI `pages/Index.ets` file with `@Entry @Component struct Index { build() { Column() { Text('hi').fontSize(20) } } }`. Renders on the simulator via the splice workflow (drop the .so + .ets into a DevEco project, click Run — DevEco's hvigor uses ets-loader to compile the ArkUI source). **New crate `crates/perry-codegen-arkts`** (~280 LOC incl. 4 unit tests): `emit_index_ets(module: &mut Module) -> Result<Option<String>>` walks `module.init` for `Stmt::Expr(NativeMethodCall { module: "perry/ui", method: "App", args: [body-shape] })`, extracts the `body:` field via `extract_body_field` (handles both `Expr::Object` AND Perry's closed-shape `Expr::New { class_name: "__AnonShape_*" }` optimization from v0.5.337+), emits ArkUI source via `emit_widget` (currently handles `Text(literal)` — other widgets degrade to a labeled placeholder Text + comment so the user sees what's unsupported), and **destructively replaces** the App-call statement with `Stmt::Expr(Expr::Number(0.0))` so codegen never sees the perry/ui call (the LLVM backend would otherwise try to emit `perry_ui_app_create` / `_set_body` / `_run` FFIs that have no `perry-ui-harmonyos` crate to link against — by design, since OHOS owns its UI tree via ArkTS). **Wiring in `compile.rs`**: harvest pass runs after the per-module post-process loop and BEFORE the i18n + codegen stages, populating `ctx.harmonyos_index_ets: Option<String>` and flipping `ctx.needs_ui` back to false (since UI is in the .ets, not the .so — releases the perry-ui-* link requirement that Phase 1's link path enforces unconditionally). The post-link `emit_harmonyos_arkts_stubs` was extended with an `index_ets: Option<&str>` parameter — when Some, it restores the `onWindowStageCreate` lifecycle hook in `EntryAbility.ets` so the UIAbility actually loads the page after `perryEntry.run()` returns (Phase 1 had dropped `onWindowStageCreate` because there was no page to load), and writes Index.ets to `<output_dir>/ets/pages/Index.ets`. **Caveats**: (1) the emitted `.ets` ships as source in the HAP because `es2abc --extension ts` rejects ArkUI decorators (`@Entry @Component struct`), and the full ets-loader pipeline needs ~15 env vars + DevEco's build-profile.json5 (deliberately avoided in B.5/v0.5.128). DevEco emulators with source-mode enabled accept this; real NEXT hardware needs ets-loader integration which is a wider follow-up. (2) Phase 2 v1 only walks the `body:` field's IMMEDIATE expression — if a user binds a widget to a local (`let t = Text("hi"); App({body: t})`) the LocalGet escape isn't followed and `t`'s nested perry/ui calls survive into codegen as unresolved FFIs. Document the inline-body restriction; broader walking is the natural Phase 2 v2 expansion. (3) Currently only `Text(literal)` is supported as a leaf widget. VStack / HStack / Button / TextField / Toggle / Slider / etc. each become one match arm in `emit_widget` + one ArkUI shape line — that's the next iteration. (4) State binding (`State<T>` reactivity) is deferred — ArkUI's `@State` / `@Link` decorators handle reactivity natively but Perry's runtime State<T> lives in the .so and doesn't share memory with the ArkTS heap; a NAPI poll/push bridge is the architectural fit. **Verified**: `cargo build --release -p perry-codegen-arkts -p perry` clean; `cargo test --release -p perry-codegen-arkts` 4/4 (empty module → None, App+Text round-trip + strip verification, unsupported-widget degradation, string escaping); end-to-end on the user's actual DevEco Studio 6.0.2 + Pura 90 Pro Max emulator: `perry compile hi.ts --target harmonyos -o /tmp/libentry.so` produces 8.9 MB ELF aarch64 OHOS .so + Index.ets with 499 bytes of valid ArkUI; splicing both into `~/DevEcoStudioProjects/MyApplication/entry/` and clicking ▶ Run renders Perry-emitted UI on the emulator (smoke test pending re-run after emulator restart — separate from this PR). The crate scaffolds on the same workspace pattern as `perry-codegen-swiftui` / `perry-codegen-glance` / `perry-codegen-wear-tiles`.

## v0.5.398 — Closes #307: `JSON.stringify(parseResult)` returned the literal string `"null"` for objects with **≥9 fields**, silently corrupting any program that round-trips JSON (perry-hub built every CI build's `job_assign` manifest as `null` for two days before the user pinned it down). Two interacting bugs in `crates/perry-runtime/src/json.rs`, both rooted in the v0.5.x inline-slot / overflow-storage split. (1) **`is_object_pointer`** at line 1395 gated stringify dispatch on `keys_len <= field_count`. Parser-built objects with ≥9 fields cap `field_count` at the inline alloc_limit (`max(field_count, 8)` physical slots — `js_object_set_field_by_name` deliberately doesn't bump field_count past inline capacity, see object.rs:2723's "Deliberately do NOT bump field_count here" comment) and store the overflow values in the `OVERFLOW_FIELDS: HashMap<usize, Vec<u64>>` thread-local at object.rs:32. So a 9-field parsed object has `keys_len=9, field_count=8`, the gate `9 <= 8` failed, and `stringify_value`'s `GC_TYPE_OBJECT` arm at json.rs:1611 fell through to the `buf.push_str("null")` else-branch — emitting the literal "null" string instead of the object. Object literals (`{a:1, b:2, ..., i:9}`) construct via `js_object_alloc_with_shape` which pre-allocates exactly N slots so `keys_len == field_count` and the gate passes — explaining why literals worked but parser output didn't. (2) Even past the gate, **`stringify_object_inner`** used `actual_fields = std::cmp::min(num_fields, keys_len)` and read fields via direct `*fields_ptr.add(f)` pointer arithmetic — only the first 8 inline slots, never the overflow map. The shape-template fast path triggered at `num_fields >= 5` had the same `min(keys_len, field_count)` bug in `build_shape_prefix_template`, so even after fixing the gate the template would emit at most 8 fields. **Three-part fix**: (a) `is_object_pointer` constraints relaxed — drop `keys_len <= field_count`, keep the bounded-size sanity checks (`keys_len <= keys_cap`, `keys_len > 0`, `keys_cap < 1000`, `field_count < 1000`). Comment explains the inline/overflow asymmetry so a future contributor doesn't accidentally re-tighten. (b) `stringify_object_inner` now uses `actual_fields = keys_len` and reads via a `read_field_bits(f)` helper that picks inline (`f < alloc_limit`) vs overflow (`crate::object::js_object_get_field(obj, f).bits()` — which already handles overflow_get fallback). The `alloc_limit = max(num_fields, 8)` invariant matches the setter's three sites (object.rs:1138, 1719, 2699). (c) Shape-template fast path skipped entirely for overflow objects via a new `has_overflow_fields = keys_len > num_fields` check before `shape_template_for(ptr)` is consulted — the template build/emit path doesn't know about overflow and would silently truncate. The slow path is fast enough for the 9-30 field range where overflow lives; the template's 7×→2× per-field win matters most for 5-8 field literal objects which still take the fast path. New regression test `test-files/test_issue_307_json_stringify_overflow_fields.ts` (8 cases — literal-9, literal-12, parse-9, parse-12, parse-8 boundary, mixed-types-with-string/null/array, dynamic obj[k]=v construction past inline cap, nested overflow objects, plus a field-access verification). Pre-fix: 9-field parsed → `"null"`. Post-fix: byte-for-byte against `node --experimental-strip-types`. **Suggested follow-up from the issue** ("make the JSON.stringify fall-through return an actual error rather than the string 'null'") deliberately deferred — that's a separate observability win whose fix shape (panic in debug, surface a unique sentinel in release, throw a TypeError) needs its own discussion thread; the pure-correctness fix here is the immediate unblocker. Verified: gap tests 27/28 = baseline (the lone fail is the pre-existing `test_gap_console_methods` ci-env quirk, unrelated); existing #154 / #212 / #302 / #304 / #305 regression tests all still match Node byte-for-byte.

## v0.5.397 — Closes #304 + #305 (two small wins from real-world repros). **#304** (`arr.length = N` doesn't truncate): `crates/perry-codegen/src/expr.rs::Expr::PropertySet` was routing every `arr.length = N` through the generic `js_object_set_field_by_name(obj, "length", N)` path which silently set a "length" key on the array's hidden object dispatch but never touched the real `ArrayHeader.length`. Result: `arr.length` reads still returned the stale original length, and the elements stayed live — broke CommandBuffer-style swap-buffer patterns where `currentCommands.length = 0` is expected to clear the buffer before re-use, leading to infinite re-processing in user code (e.g. @codehz/ecs `CommandBuffer.execute`). Fix in two parts: (1) new runtime FFI `js_array_set_length(arr, new_length: f64)` in `crates/perry-runtime/src/array.rs` that truncates by clearing elements [n..cur) to TAG_UNDEFINED + setting `length=n`, OR extends in-place when `n <= capacity`, OR calls `js_array_grow(arr, n)` when `n > capacity` (the v0.5.x `js_array_grow` already installs a forwarding pointer at the OLD location via the issue #233 mechanism, so the caller's stale pointer transparently follows the chain). NaN/negative/non-integer clamp to 0 (spec says RangeError; clamping is a known gap worth a follow-up). (2) New codegen arm in `Expr::PropertySet` at line 2700 (before any other dispatch) detects `property == "length" && is_array_expr(ctx, object)` and emits a `js_array_set_length` call. Dynamic `Any`-typed receivers that happen to be arrays at runtime still hit the generic path — runtime-side detection inside `js_object_set_field_by_name` is the natural follow-up but deliberately out of scope here; the static-typed case covers the issue's repro. **#305** (`const m = this.map; for-of m` yields zero iterations): v0.5.388's #302 fix added `class_field_types` registry + `lookup_class_field_type` so the for-of source resolver could see `this.<field>: Map<K,V>`. But the local-alias case `const m = this.map` runs through `infer_type_from_expr` (`crates/perry-hir/src/lower_types.rs::ast::Expr::Member`) which had no `this.<field>` arm — fell through `_ => Type::Any`. Result: `m`'s declared local type was `Any`, the for-of fell off the Map fast path, and produced `iterCount=0` plus key-bits-as-numbers garbage from `Array.from(m.keys())`. Same shape for `const s = this.items; for-of s` on a class Set field, and `const a = this.xs` on a class number[] field — all three suffered the same misdispatch. Fix: 4-line addition to the Member arm — when `member.obj` is `Expr::This` AND `ctx.current_class.is_some()`, consult `ctx.lookup_class_field_type(class, prop)` and return that type if registered; otherwise fall through to the existing arm. Same registry the #302 fix populated; this just wires up the second consumer. New regression tests `test-files/test_issue_304_array_length_set.ts` (7 cases — truncate to 0 / truncate to 2 / no-op / extend in-capacity / push after truncate / string array / CommandBuffer swap-buffer pattern from issue) and `test-files/test_issue_305_local_alias_class_field_map.ts` (4 cases — Map local alias, Map this.x direct comparison, Set local alias, Array local alias). Both match `node --experimental-strip-types` byte-for-byte. Verified: gap tests 27/28 = baseline; existing regression tests for #154 / #212 / #302 still pass byte-for-byte.

## v0.5.396 — Closes #245 Phase 2: workspace-wide `cargo clippy --fix` auto-correction sweep. 132 files touched, +1314/-1648 = -334 LOC net. Categorically: ~43× `std::mem::transmute::<i64, f64>(x)` → `f64::from_bits(i64::cast_unsigned(x))` (NaN-boxing idiom modernization — equivalence-preserving), ~22 unneeded `return` statement removals, ~5 manual `RangeInclusive::contains` rewrites, ~10 manual `div_ceil` rewrites, ~5 `is_multiple_of` rewrites, ~57 `Cell::new(...)`/`Vec::new(...)`/`Box::new(...)` simplifications, plus various small idiom-modernizations (`std::mem::take`, `std::iter::repeat_n`, `std::env::var`, etc.). Also runs `cargo fmt --all` over the whole workspace so the lint gate stays green. Excluded the 7 platform-specific UI crates (perry-ui-ios/tvos/watchos/visionos/android/windows/gtk4) since they don't build on the macOS host where clippy was run; their auto-fixes can be applied separately by anyone with the SDK. Excluded `clippy::not_unsafe_ptr_arg_deref` (`-A` flag during the sweep) — 300 instances are `pub extern "C" fn` FFI surface that's unsafe by contract; marking them all `unsafe` would mean the codegen-emitted IR has to wrap every call site in `unsafe {}`, which it can't because the calls come from raw LLVM `call` instructions, not Rust code. Phase 1 (the `cargo clippy --check -D warnings` gate) is the natural next step but is left for a focused follow-up since 300 ptr-arg-deref errors need a project-wide allow directive in `clippy.toml` first; doing both in one commit would muddy the auto-fix audit trail. **Verified**: cargo build --release clean; cargo test --workspace 458/0 = baseline + the 2 v0.5.395 perry updater unit tests; cargo fmt --check clean; perry-updater test surface unchanged. **No code change beyond mechanical clippy auto-fixes; no parity change; no functional behavior change.**

## v0.5.395 — Closes the loop on #229: sign-side CLI tool for v2 manifest signatures. v0.5.391 shipped the verify-side `perry_updater_verify_signature_v2` runtime FFI but deferred sign-side tooling — apps could verify v2 sigs but had to roll their own ed25519 + sha256 + payload-build code to produce them. Three new subcommands under `perry updater`: (1) **`keygen`** generates a fresh Ed25519 keypair via `OsRng` (rand 0.9 `try_fill_bytes`), emits `{public_key, secret_key}` JSON with base64-encoded byte strings; on Unix sets the output file to mode 0600 best-effort so the secret isn't world-readable. (2) **`sign`** computes `Ed25519(sha256(binary) || version_utf8)` exactly like the runtime verify path (`crates/perry-updater/src/core.rs:264`) and emits a JSON envelope `{schemaVersion: 2, version, size, sha256, signature, publicKey}` that drops cleanly into a manifest entry via `jq -s`. Two key-input modes: `--secret-key <path>` reads the JSON file produced by keygen, or `--secret-key-b64 <inline>` for CI where the secret comes from a repository secret without hitting the worker filesystem. Empty version is rejected up-front (matches the verify-side invariant — `payload = digest || ""` would collapse to a v1 signature). (3) **`verify`** runs the same algorithm the runtime uses, intended as a CI-side sanity check before uploading the manifest; takes `--binary --version --signature --pubkey` and exits 0 / 1 on pass / fail. New `crates/perry/src/commands/updater.rs` (372 LOC including unit tests) wired into `crates/perry/src/main.rs::Commands::Updater` + `is_legacy_invocation` known-subcommand list. New direct deps in `crates/perry/Cargo.toml`: `ed25519-dalek = "2.1"` (with `rand_core` feature so `OsRng` integrates), `sha2 = "0.10"`, `hex = "0.4"`, `rand = "0.9"` — all already in the workspace's transitive link surface via perry-stdlib's crypto feature, so no actual new crates pulled in. Two unit tests: (a) `keygen_sign_verify_roundtrip` — full keygen → sign → verify cycle through the actual command entrypoints, plus a tampered-version negative case that asserts the verify fails; (b) `empty_version_rejected` — pins the spec invariant. Doc-update at `docs/src/updater/overview.md` adds a "Sign-side CLI (v0.5.395+)" section with the three-step recipe (keygen → sign → verify) and a CI-tip on the `--secret-key-b64` env-var pattern. **Verified end-to-end** by `cargo build --release -p perry` then `perry updater keygen --output kp.json` → `perry updater sign --binary x.bin --version 1.2.3 --secret-key kp.json` → `perry updater verify ... → OK`; tampered version `--version 9.9.9` with the same signature returns `signature error: Verification equation was not satisfied` and exits 1. Unit tests 2/2 pass under `cargo test --bin perry commands::updater`.

## v0.5.394 — v0.5.393 cargo-test follow-up: also exclude `perry-jsruntime` from `cargo test --workspace` on ubuntu-latest. v0.5.393's `--exclude perry-ui-macos` fix got past the objc2 wall but exposed a deeper duplicate-symbol issue in the perry-jsruntime test binary itself. The 12 V8 FFI symbols (`js_load_module`, `js_call_function`, `js_get_export`, `js_set_property`, `js_runtime_init`, `js_new_from_handle`, `js_new_instance`, `js_create_callback`, `js_await_js_promise`, `js_await_any_promise`, `js_handle_array_get`, `js_handle_array_length`) are defined twice when linking the perry-jsruntime test binary on Linux: as strong stubs in `crates/perry-runtime/src/closure.rs` (gated `cfg(not(target_os = "macos"))` — Linux falls into this branch) AND as real implementations in `crates/perry-jsruntime/src/interop.rs`. macOS sidesteps this via the `core::arch::global_asm!` `.weak_definition` block at closure.rs:1549+ (only fires on `target_os = "macos", target_arch = "aarch64"`); Linux ELF would need either nightly's `#[linkage = "weak"]` or hand-rolled `.weak` directives in inline asm — a separate refactor, not blocking this CI migration. The exclusion is also consistent with v0.5.297's finding that perry-jsruntime tests are independently flaky on Linux due to V8/deno_core threading conflicts. Comment block in `test.yml` explicitly walks future contributors through both the link-time problem and the runtime-time finding so the pattern is discoverable. **No code change; no parity change; CI workflow change only.**

## v0.5.393 — Release-night reliability + v0.5.392 follow-up. **(1) Release-packages publish-job sweep**: extends the v0.5.386 workflow_dispatch fallback pattern (which was previously only on the `Upload release asset` step) to all 5 publish jobs in `.github/workflows/release-packages.yml` — `homebrew`, `apt`, `apt-repo`, `winget`, `update-workers`. Pre-fix, each job's `if: github.event_name == 'release'` gate would silently skip the entire job whenever the release was triggered manually via `workflow_dispatch` (the fallback path used during v0.5.386 release night when the original `release`-event run failed at await-tests and the user re-fired the workflow as workflow_dispatch). Result on v0.5.386: binaries uploaded successfully (the upload step already had the fallback), but Homebrew, apt repository, winget manifests, and the worker-update notification all silently no-op'd. Same fix applied 5×: (1) `if:` gate widened from `github.event_name == 'release'` to `github.event_name == 'release' || github.event_name == 'workflow_dispatch'`. (2) Each job's "Get release info" / "Get release version" step gains a `gh release list --limit 1 --json tagName` fallback when `github.event.release.tag_name` is empty (workflow_dispatch context doesn't populate that field). (3) `GH_TOKEN: ${{ secrets.GITHUB_TOKEN }}` env added to each step so `gh release list` can authenticate. Bash sites use `[ -z "$TAG" ]` + `gh release list ... --jq '.[0].tagName'`; the winget job's PowerShell version uses `if (-not $tag) { ... }` mirroring its existing structure. The `npm-publish` job at line 736 already had a workflow_dispatch arm via `inputs.publish_npm == 'true'` and didn't need editing. Pre-existing `release`-event behavior unchanged (the fallback only fires when `github.event.release.tag_name` is empty, which it never is on release events). YAML validates clean. **(2) cargo-test ubuntu fix**: v0.5.392's macOS→ubuntu migration of the `cargo-test` job in `test.yml` failed CI because the existing `--exclude` list only filtered platform-specific UI crates that don't build on macOS — it never excluded `perry-ui-macos` itself. On macos-14 that was fine; on ubuntu, `perry-ui-macos`'s transitive `objc2` dep emits `compile_error!("`objc2` only works on Apple platforms")` and the cargo-test job died at the dep-graph compile step before any test ran. Added `--exclude perry-ui-macos` to the test command and updated the comment block to reflect the ubuntu reality (objc2 gates all 5 Apple UI crates, not the SDK availability that was the original macos-14 reason for excluding ios/tvos/watchos). gtk4 stays excluded — wiring it in needs an `apt-get install libgtk-4-dev` step which is a separate follow-up. parity + compile-smoke jobs are unaffected because they run `cargo build --release` which only compiles `workspace.default-members` (no objc2 anywhere in that closure). **No code change; no parity change; CI workflow change only.**

## v0.5.392 — CI cost reduction: move `cargo-test`, `parity`, and `compile-smoke` jobs from `macos-14` (10× billing weight) → `ubuntu-latest` (1×) in `.github/workflows/test.yml`. None of the three exercise platform-specific behavior — cargo-test's `--exclude` list already filters every macOS-only UI crate (perry-ui-{ios,visionos,tvos,watchos,gtk4,android,windows}); parity is plain `node` stdout-vs-`perry` stdout diffing; compile-smoke runs the bare `perry foo.ts -o out` path which doesn't link any platform UI lib. The v0.5.385 portable-sha256 fix already routes through `command -v sha256sum || shasum -a 256` so works on Linux's GNU coreutils + BSD shasum hosts alike. `gtimeout`-vs-`timeout` is auto-detected by `run_parity_tests.sh` (`command -v gtimeout || timeout`). Node 22+ is installed via setup-node@v4 below the `runs-on:` line. Stale macOS disk-cleanup comment blocks (`macos-14 ships with ~14 GB free disk after the preinstalled Xcode + iOS/tvOS/watchOS simulator runtime images...`) removed — that was the rationale for the simulator-runtime-IMAGES wipe step which Linux runners don't need. NJOBS=3 retained conservatively (Linux runners have 4 vCPUs vs macos-14's 3, but the cargo auto-optimize race is independent of vCPU count and the issue is tracked separately for future flock-based recovery to NJOBS=6). Lint + binary-size jobs deliberately stay on `macos-14`: lint runs `cargo fmt --check` once and is fast regardless; binary-size measures macOS-binary-specific output and would lose its meaning on Linux. Doc-tests + simctl-tests already use a matrix that includes ubuntu-24.04 and macos-14 explicitly — those are the host-platform-specific jobs and remain unchanged. Expected savings: 3 jobs × 10× billing weight × ~10-20 min each = the bulk of the per-PR CI cost. **No test changes; no parity changes; not user-visible.** Verified: `python3 -c "import yaml; yaml.safe_load(...)"` on the modified file is clean.

## v0.5.391 — Closes #229: version-binding into the perry-updater signed payload (Option A from the design comment). Pre-fix the signed payload was just the raw 32-byte SHA-256 digest of the binary — the version string was unsigned. An on-path attacker could serve a tampered manifest pairing a previously-signed older binary's URL + signature with a higher version number; the running client would download the binary, verify SHA-256 (matches — it's the real older binary), verify signature against the pinned pubkey (matches — it really WAS signed), install + relaunch, and get pushed to a known-vulnerable version. **Fix**: new `perry_updater_verify_signature_v2(file_path, sig, pubkey, version)` FFI in `crates/perry-updater/src/core.rs` that builds the signed payload as `digest_bytes (32) || version_utf8 (variable)` and verifies that. Empty version is rejected up-front (would otherwise collapse to v1 payload and let any v1 signature pass v2 verify). Manifest `schemaVersion` bumped 1 → 2 to signal which verify path the client should take; the @perry/updater wrapper accepts both v1 and v2 manifests, dispatching on `manifest.schemaVersion` to either `verifySignature` (legacy, digest-only) or `verifySignatureV2` (recommended, version-bound). New ambient TS export `verifySignatureV2` at `types/perry/updater/index.d.ts`. New dispatch row in `crates/perry-dispatch/src/lib.rs` next to the v1 row. New comprehensive unit test `signature_verify_v2_roundtrip_and_replay_defense` (10 → 11 perry-updater tests passing, 0/0 failing): asserts (1) v2 sig+matching version verifies, (2) **old-binary replay defense** — a v1-style sig (digest only) MUST NOT verify against the v2 path even when the version label matches, (3) tampered version label fails, (4) tampered binary fails, (5) empty-version is rejected. Migration story documented in `docs/src/updater/overview.md`: v0.5.391+ clients accept both schemaVersion 1 and 2; deploys must update clients via a v1 manifest first, THEN bump to v2 manifests, since older v1-only clients reject v2 with `unsupported manifest schemaVersion`. Trust-model section in the docs rewritten to lead with the v2 (recommended) flow + show the v1 (legacy + vulnerable) flow as backwards-compat. Sign-side CLI tooling for v2 deferred to a follow-up — not blocking the verify-side hardening; existing apps can build v2 signatures with any Ed25519 library by computing `sha256(binary) + version.encode("utf-8")` and signing that. The full design comment posted on issue #229 covers the Option-A vs Option-B (manifest signing) tradeoff and the rejected Option-D (boot-side runtime version verification — worth doing later as defense-in-depth, but Option A alone closes the documented attack).

## v0.5.390 — Closes #228: enforce HTTPS on `@perry/updater`'s manifest + asset URLs. Pre-fix `packages/perry-updater/src/index.ts::checkForUpdate` and `downloadAndVerify` accepted `http://` URLs without complaint, leaving updates vulnerable to (a) **update suppression** (passive on-path attacker rewrites the manifest fetch to claim "you're already up to date", indefinitely keeping the user on a stale version with known CVEs) and (b) **privacy leak** (manifest URL leaks app + currently-installed version over plaintext). Signature pinning protects integrity but neither of these vectors. New `assertSecureUrl(url, kind)` validator parses via `new URL(url)` and rejects any scheme that's not `https:` — except for `http://` on loopback hosts (`127.0.0.1`, `::1`, `localhost`), which are explicitly allowed because `scripts/smoke_updater.{sh,ps1}` serve test manifests from `http://127.0.0.1:$PORT`. Wired into `checkForUpdate` (validates `opts.manifestUrl`) and `downloadAndVerify` (validates each `asset.url` from the manifest). Error messages include the schema we got + the workarounds (use https://, or loopback for local testing). JSDoc on `UpdaterOptions.manifestUrl` updated from "Manifest URL (HTTPS)" → an explicit MUST-be-HTTPS-with-loopback-exception spec referencing #228. **#229 (version-binding into signed payload to prevent old-binary replay) deferred to a focused PR** — the change is bigger than #228 (sign-side CLI tooling + manifest schemaVersion 1→2 + verify-side FFI signature change + migration story) and warrants careful design rather than rushing it on top of #228. Posted full Option-A design + acceptance criteria + 4-6h cost estimate as a comment on the issue. Both #228 fix and #229 design land tonight; the actual #229 implementation will be its own PR. Total: 167/167 parity preserved (no parity surface touched), perry-updater test surface unchanged for HTTPS callers, smoke tests still pass against http://127.0.0.1.

## v0.5.389 — Closes #300 (Windows SDK auto-discovery) + cosmetic cleanup for #266. **#300 was a non-default-Windows-install bug**: a user with VS installed on D: hit `LINK : fatal error LNK1181: cannot open input file "user32.lib"` because `find_msvc_lib_paths()` in `crates/perry/src/commands/compile/library_search.rs:317` hardcoded the Windows SDK lib lookup to `C:\Program Files (x86)\Windows Kits\10\Lib`. The MSVC CRT lookup via `vswhere` correctly finds the user's D:-installed VS, but the SDK path probe is purely a hardcoded `read_dir`, so when the SDK lives elsewhere (or the default path is empty / has no SDK version subdir), `find_msvc_lib_paths` silently returns ONLY the MSVC CRT path and link.exe can't find `user32.lib` in `LIB` → `LNK1181`. Pre-fix the failure was silent — no `perry doctor` warning, no informative error. **Three-layer fix**: (1) probe a list of candidate SDK roots in priority order: registry `HKLM\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows Kits\Installed Roots\KitsRoot10` (the canonical source — what `vcvars64.bat` consults), then `%ProgramFiles%`, then `%ProgramFiles(x86)%`, then the legacy hardcoded path as a final fallback. New `read_registry_kits_root_10()` helper shells out to `reg query` (keeps perry build dep-free; same result as the `winreg` crate but no Cargo.toml change). (2) Stop on first SDK that has a `<ver>\um\x64` subdirectory — both `um\x64` (user32, kernel32, etc.) and `ucrt\x64` (CRT) get added. (3) Fail LOUD when no SDK was found AND `LIB` env var isn't set: print a `Warning: Windows SDK lib path ... not found` block listing every candidate path tried + the three workarounds (run `vcvars64.bat`, install Windows 10/11 SDK via VS Installer, set `LIB` manually). Pre-fix users got a confusing `LNK1181` from link.exe; now they get an actionable Perry-side message before the linker even runs. Diagnosis credit: research subagent — found the single hardcoded `Windows Kits\10\Lib` reference in the entire codebase, confirmed via the user's vswhere output that VS detection works fine and SDK is the only remaining input to `LIB`. **Cosmetic #266 cleanup**: stale doc-comment at `crates/perry-runtime/src/promise.rs:1427` said "Promise.any rejects with an array of rejection reasons (Perry doesn't have AggregateError yet)" — actually since the v0.5.x runtime work that landed for #256 / #283 / etc., the all-rejected path DOES construct an `AggregateError` via `js_aggregate_error_new` at `promise.rs:1558`. Updated comment to reflect reality. Issue #266 closed: a parallel research subagent verified all 4 sub-bugs are now fixed end-to-end (`new Promise(executor)` body fires synchronously, `Promise.any` works incl. all-rejected → AggregateError, `.then(p => Promise)` thenable unwrap from #256 generalizes to all .then callbacks, `.finally().then()` value passing preserves the upstream value via the `next = null` + extra-tick passthrough). All 4 sub-bug repros now produce empty diff vs Node. **Stats**: 167/167 parity rate maintained (was 100% in v0.5.388, stays 100%); the 5 closed issues since v0.5.380 are #154, #237, #244, #266, #278, #291, #302; remaining open: #300 (closing now via this commit), #228 / #229 / #243 / #242 / #230 / #210 / #99 / #100 / #131 / #76 / #115 / #113 / #245 / #272 / #273. Diagnosis was via 3 parallel research subagents — one for Promise (#266) returned "all 4 already fixed", one for #300 found the hardcoded Windows SDK path, one for #245 (clippy) returned a categorization showing Phase-1 gate landing requires Phase-2 auto-fix to come first (commented on the issue). All 3 ran concurrently in roughly 10 minutes total, would have been ~1.5 hours sequentially.

## v0.5.388 — Two real bug fixes that flipped the last 2 entries from `known_failures.json` to passing — Perry's parity rate is now 100% (167/167) and gap tests are 27/28 (only `console_methods` remains, a long-documented ci-env quirk). **#302** (NEW today): `for...of` over a Map/Set held in a class instance field silently skipped the loop body. The for-of HIR lowering at `crates/perry-hir/src/lower_decl.rs:3627` and `crates/perry-hir/src/lower.rs:5377` only resolved iterable types via `lookup_local_type` — meaning the `Ident` case worked (`for (const x of localMap)`) but the `Member { obj: This, prop: ident }` case (`for (const x of this.classMap)`) fell through to a raw Map handle that the for-loop's `.length` read returned 0 on. Fix is a parallel `class_field_types: Vec<(String, Vec<(String, Type)>)>` registry alongside the existing `class_field_names`, populated from each class's declared `ClassProp` `type_ann` in an early-pass loop BEFORE method bodies are lowered (mirrors the existing static-fields-early-pass at line ~636 — order matters because methods reference fields). New `register_class_field_types` + `lookup_class_field_type` helpers next to the field-names ones. Both for-of arms refactored to share an `iterable_type: Option<Type>` resolver that handles both `Ident → lookup_local_type` and `Member { obj: This, prop } → lookup_class_field_type` shapes; the existing Map/Set/Array element-type propagation downstream now reads from the resolved `iterable_type` instead of re-doing the Ident lookup. Also added the missing `Set` arm in `lower_decl.rs` (the `lower.rs` site already had it; the `lower_decl.rs` site only handled Map). New regression test `test-files/test_issue_302_class_field_for_of.ts` (3 cases — declared+initialized field, declared field initialized in ctor, deeper iteration with multi-line body) matches `node --experimental-strip-types` byte-for-byte. **#154** (pre-existing SIGBUS — acknowledged in CLAUDE.md v0.5.377): `await using r = new R()` where `R[Symbol.asyncDispose]() { await new Promise(...) }` segfaulted with `EXC_BAD_ACCESS code=2` at `crates/perry-runtime/src/box.rs:64::js_box_set`'s `str d0, [x0]` instruction. **Root cause**: `compute_max_func_id` in `crates/perry-transform/src/generator.rs:313` only walked `module.functions ∪ module.init` — but **NOT `module.classes`** — when finding the max FuncId in use. The async-dispose method's executor closure `(r) => setTimeout(r, 1)` lives inside `class.methods[i].body` and carries a real FuncId (e.g. 3). The generator transform's `next_func_id = max + 1` calculation undercounts, then mints the synthesized iterator's `return` method as the same FuncId 3 — colliding with the user's executor. At codegen, the iterator-return body wins; `js_promise_new_with_executor(closure_3)` invokes the iterator-return with `arg = resolve` and 0 captures. The body reads `js_closure_get_capture_f64(this_closure, 2)` past the 0-cap end, gets a code-segment pointer, and `js_box_set(that_pointer, TAG_TRUE)` writes a double to read-only `__TEXT` → SIGBUS. **Fix**: mirror the v0.5.323 class-scan that the SIBLING `compute_max_local_id` got for issue #212 — append a class-walk loop after the existing `module.functions` and `module.init` walks, scanning `class.{methods, static_methods, constructor, getters, setters}.body`. Verified end-to-end: `test-files/test_issue_154_using_dispose.ts` now matches Node byte-for-byte (sync + multi-binding + null-skip + async cases). Both fixes triaged in `known_failures.json` are now removed; the file is empty `{}` for the first time since the file was introduced. Diagnosis credit: research subagents A (#302) and B (#154) — A found the gate-on-Ident root cause via HIR diff, B used `lldb` to capture the crashing instruction (`str d0, [x0]` at `js_box_set`) and the IR dump showed `js_promise_new_with_executor(@perry_closure_3, 0 captures)` where closure_3's body was the iterator-return template. Both fixes are minimal mirrors of existing patterns (the static-name early-pass for #302, the v0.5.323 LocalId fix for #154). Verified: cargo build --release clean; gap tests 27/28 = previous baseline +1 (typed_arrays flipped); parity sweep 167/167 = 100%; existing #212, #221, #233, #235, #261, #263 regression tests still match Node byte-for-byte.

## v0.5.387 — CI overhaul (post-mortem from v0.5.386's painful release night). Three connected workflow changes: (1) **`release-packages.yml::await-tests`** got two fixes: bump the per-workflow deadline 45 min → 60 min (Tests on macos-14 routinely takes 50+ min wall, so 45 min was a coin flip; 60 min still well under GitHub's 6h workflow timeout) AND switch the API query from `per_page=1` → `per_page=20` + jq filter for `select(.conclusion == "success")` so the gate finds ANY green run on the SHA instead of locking to the newest (which might be in_progress while an older run on the same SHA was already green). The v0.5.386 cycle hit this twice — once from a tag-push Tests run obscuring a green main-push run, once after force-tag-move from a brand-new in-progress run. Also added a "FAIL if every completed run on this SHA failed" arm so the gate fails fast on consistent failures instead of waiting out the full 60 min for transient ones. (2) **Drop the `build` job from `test.yml`**: it produced `target/release/perry` + `libperry_runtime.a` + `libperry_stdlib.a` artifacts that NOTHING downstream consumed except `binary-size` (which is `if: refs/heads/main` only). cargo-test / parity / compile-smoke / doc-tests each did their own `cargo build --release` anyway, so `needs: build` was a 6-7 min serializing barrier with zero cache benefit. Now those four jobs start in parallel directly off `actions/checkout@v4`. `binary-size` does its own targeted `cargo build --release -p perry -p perry-runtime -p perry-stdlib` (replaces the dropped artifact download). Net: ~7 min wall-clock savings on every PR run + simpler workflow graph. (3) **Replace `actions/cache@v4` with `Swatinem/rust-cache@v2`** across all 6 jobs (lint, cargo-test, parity, compile-smoke, doc-tests, binary-size). Pre-fix the cache deliberately skipped `target/` because manual `actions/cache@v4` of the full `target/` would push macOS-14's ~14 GB free disk over the limit (the explicit "deliberately NOT caching `target/`" comment in 6 places attested to the workaround). Swatinem caches `target/` smartly — pruning intermediate compile artifacts that don't help warm builds, keeping only dep packages + meaningful incremental state — so the typical cache size stays under 1 GB. Now warm builds get the actual target-dir benefit. `save-if: github.ref == 'refs/heads/main'` ensures PRs read from cache but only main writes new entries, avoiding cache thrash from short-lived branches. The "Free up disk space (macOS)" simulator-runtime wipe step is dropped from cargo-test / parity / compile-smoke / binary-size (Swatinem's pruning means the disk-pressure problem doesn't recur); kept in doc-tests since it does heavy multi-crate cross-compile work that could still expand `target/` past safe limits. Combined: Tests workflow ~40 min wall → expected ~25-30 min on warm cache, ~33 min on cold. Build job's 6m25s previously serial-blocking 4 downstream jobs is now eliminated entirely; cargo-test (4m), parity (15m), compile-smoke (10m, NJOBS=3), doc-tests (28-50m) all run in parallel from t=0. The 4 docs/Linux/Windows runs in our v0.5.386 release cycle each consumed roughly 20 macOS-14 minutes for the build job alone — multiplied by the 5 retries that night, this single change recovers ~8 macOS-14 hours per future release cycle. CI hygiene only — no version bump on user-facing surface; bumped 0.5.386 → 0.5.387 per the maintainer convention.

## v0.5.386 — Hotfix: v0.5.385's new HIR arm for `module.Class.staticMethod()` over-fired and broke `fs.promises.readFile()` (and likely `fs.promises.writeFile/mkdir/access/...` + `fs.constants.X` + `path.posix.X` + `path.win32.X`). The arm I added at `crates/perry-hir/src/lower/expr_call.rs` after the `process.hrtime.bigint()` handler matched ANY `module.X.method()` shape on a registered native module, intercepting `fs.promises.readFile(...)` and emitting `NativeMethodCall { module: "fs", class_name: Some("promises"), method: "readFile", ... }`. That new HIR shape doesn't match the existing dedicated codegen arm in `crates/perry-codegen/src/expr.rs:7881` (which expects the unmodified `Call { callee: PropertyGet { object: PropertyGet { object: NativeModuleRef("fs"), property: "promises" }, property: "readFile" }, ... }` shape) and instead falls into `lower_call/native.rs:480`'s `_ => eprintln!("perry-codegen: unhandled fs.{}() NativeMethodCall ({})", method, ...)` warn-and-undef path. Result: `await fs.promises.readFile(file, 'utf-8')` silently returned `undefined`, surfacing in CI as `test_gap_node_fs` parity failure on the v0.5.385 / v0.5.384 Tests run (line 20 of the test diff: `Node: true / Perry: false` for `promiseResult === testContent`). Diagnosed via `--print-hir` showing the new (broken) NativeMethodCall shape; reproduced minimally in 5 lines (`const r = await fs.promises.readFile(f, 'utf-8'); console.log(typeof r)` → `undefined`). **Fix**: add a `is_sub_namespace` exclusion list to the v0.5.385 arm covering `("fs", "promises")`, `("fs", "constants")`, `("path", "posix")`, `("path", "win32")` so the existing dedicated codegen arms keep handling those shapes. The new arm still fires for `ethers.Wallet.createRandom()` and any future `module.RealClass.staticMethod()` pattern; just not for sub-namespace patterns. Verified locally: minimal repro now prints `XYZ / typeof: string` (correct), full parity sweep now reports 166 pass / 1 fail (only `test_issue_154_using_dispose` which is in `known_failures.json` with `status: "bug"`). The list is intentionally explicit (not a heuristic) to keep the behavior predictable: every new sub-namespace gets a dedicated entry. Could be replaced with a codegen-layer `NATIVE_MODULE_TABLE` lookup at HIR time but that pulls in a cross-crate dep that's not worth the complexity for the current 4 entries. Frustrating debug detail: my first build after the fix didn't pick up the change because `target/perry-auto-<hash>/release/libperry_runtime.a` was cached from the pre-fix run — the fix is in perry-codegen which IS rebuilt by `cargo build -p perry`, but the auto-optimize cargo cache keys off feature-set hash, not source mtime. Adding `PERRY_NO_CACHE=1` to the test invocation produced the correct output. Same trap any future contributor will hit; mentioned here so it's findable by grep.

## v0.5.385 — Closes #278 (PR #299, manually rebased + landed): wire codegen dispatch for the 3 perry/system + ethers holdouts that #278 documented. **`getLocale` / `getAppIcon`** (perry/system) — both runtime FFIs were already implemented across every platform crate (`perry_system_get_locale()` + `perry_system_get_app_icon(i64)`) but had no rows in `PERRY_SYSTEM_TABLE` (`crates/perry-dispatch/src/lib.rs`), so user-side calls reached the receiver-less early-out at `lower_call.rs:2849-2854` and silently returned `undefined`. Added 2 `MethodRow`s with `args/ret` shapes derived from the FFI signatures (`getLocale: [] → Str`, `getAppIcon: [Str] → Widget`). **`ethers.Wallet.createRandom()`** — three-part wiring: (1) HIR lowering at `crates/perry-hir/src/lower/expr_call.rs` got a new handler matching the `module.Class.staticMethod()` shape (outer Member → inner Member → Ident → native-module lookup), modelled after the existing `process.hrtime.bigint()` block; produces `NativeMethodCall { module, class_name: Some(class_name), method, ... }` for any 2-deep static call on a native module class. (2) Runtime FFI `js_ethers_wallet_create_random()` in `crates/perry-stdlib/src/ethers.rs` generates a 32-byte cryptorandom private key via `rand::thread_rng`, derives the 20-byte Ethereum address as `keccak256(pk)[12..32]`, applies EIP-55 checksum, and returns a JS object with `address` + `privateKey` string fields. (3) Dispatch rows added to `NATIVE_MODULE_TABLE` in `crates/perry-codegen/src/lower_call.rs` for the full ethers utility surface — `getAddress`, `formatEther`, `formatUnits`, `parseEther`, `parseUnits`, plus `createRandom` with `class_filter: Some("Wallet")`. New `NativeRetKind::BigInt` variant (already declared in the enum, just unused before) lets `parseEther`/`parseUnits` NaN-box their `*mut BigIntHeader` returns with BIGINT_TAG (0x7FFA). Docs caught up too: `docs/src/stdlib/crypto.md` flips from "not yet wired" → live `{{#include}}` extract; new `ethers` anchor block in `docs/examples/stdlib/crypto/snippets.ts`; new `locale` + `app-icon` anchors in `docs/examples/system/snippets.ts`; TS surface `getLocale` + `getAppIcon` declarations added to `types/perry/system/index.d.ts`. **Manual rebase notes**: PR #299 was opened against `ea95e858` (pre-v0.5.382), conflicted on 4 files when the v0.5.382 + v0.5.384 stack landed (`lower_call.rs` + `dispatch/lib.rs` + `expr_call.rs` + `ethers.rs`). Rebased manually onto current main: dispatch table conflict was just multi-line vs compact rustfmt style (kept multi-line for consistency with existing rows + appended the 2 new rows in the same style); lower_call.rs conflicts were 3 small chunks (use-stmt union, NativeRetKind::BigInt arm + reformatted F64 arm, ethers section appended verbatim with style normalization); expr_call.rs's giant 592-line conflict marker was misleading — branch's actual diff was just 24 surgical lines added near `process.hrtime` block, so I took main's version verbatim and inserted the new block at the right spot. ethers.rs conflict was just the `use` statement union. `cargo check -p perry-codegen -p perry-hir -p perry-dispatch -p perry-stdlib` clean post-resolution. PR #299 author attribution preserved on the rebased commit; this v0.5.385 bump + changelog entry amended on top per the maintainer-merge convention.

## v0.5.384 — CI hotfix-of-hotfix: with v0.5.383's nullglob fix actually landed, the compile-smoke run on 0bdccbd4 successfully printed `Compile smoke: 183 passed, 1 failed, 4 skipped` — and the lone failure surfaced a **separate race condition I introduced via parallelization** (NJOBS=6 was too aggressive for the 3-vCPU macos-14 runner). One test (`test_edge_enums_const`) hit `ld: file cannot be open()ed, errno=2 path=.../target/perry-auto-727478db4b75c4fb/release/libperry_runtime.a`: two parallel workers both wanted the same auto-optimize feature combo's `libperry_runtime.a`. Worker A was mid-rebuild (deletes-then-writes the .a), worker B's perry had already finished its cargo build and invoked clang to link, clang opened the .a in the brief deleted window and bailed. Race window is sub-second so it didn't surface on my 12-core local Mac (NJOBS=6 finished cleanly in 2m 21s for 187 files locally), but on macos-14's 3-vCPU runner with longer cargo lock contention it's reachable. Two-line fix: (1) **drop `NJOBS` default 6 → 3** (matches macos-14's vCPU count, reduces race likelihood since fewer concurrent cargo invocations contend for the same auto-optimize cache dir). (2) **Add a single retry-after-2s** to `compile_one`: `if "$PERRY" "$f" -o ... 2>"$err_log" || (sleep 2 && "$PERRY" "$f" -o ... 2>"$err_log"); then`. The `||` short-circuits on first success so the success path is unchanged; the 2s sleep gives the racing worker time to finish writing the .a before the retry. Belt-and-suspenders: the lower NJOBS makes the race rare, the retry handles whatever still slips through. Sequential baseline was ~26 min; expect ~10-12 min at NJOBS=3 (vs ~6-8 min at NJOBS=6 with the race). Acceptable trade — green CI is worth 4 min. Long-term proper fix would be perry-side: hold a flock on `target/perry-auto-<hash>/.lock` during BOTH the rebuild AND the link, so workers in the same feature combo serialize while different combos still run in parallel. Tracked separately as a perry follow-up; out of scope for this CI hotfix sequence.

## v0.5.383 — CI hotfix: my v0.5.381 nullglob fix for the compile-smoke errexit bug **never actually landed in 72d17ff8** — the diff hunk that replaced `PASS=$(ls -1 *.pass | wc -l)` with `shopt -s nullglob; pass_files=("$LOGS_DIR"/*.pass); PASS=${#pass_files[@]}` got separated from the v0.5.381 commit and ended up sitting in a `git stash` (`stash@{0}: On main: compile-smoke nullglob fix (preserved post-#294)`). The v0.5.381 commit only contained the parity jq filter + docs fence tagging + known_failures.json triage; the actual compile-smoke fix never reached main. First confirmation: rerun #25116455705's compile-smoke job at ea95e858 (which has v0.5.381's commit in its ancestry) failed with the EXACT same symptom as the v0.5.379 baseline — last test compiled at `Wrote executable: /tmp/perry_smoke_test_tls_connect`, then immediately `##[error]Process completed with exit code 1`, no "Compile smoke: X passed..." summary line ever printed, no error logs uploaded (`No files were found with the provided path: /tmp/perry_smoke_logs/*.compile_error.log`). Verified by `git show 72d17ff8 -- .github/workflows/test.yml` showing only the parity-job hunk + by `grep ls -1.*pass .github/workflows/test.yml` returning the unchanged broken line at 405. **Fix**: `git stash pop stash@{0}` to recover the nullglob hunk + commit it as v0.5.383. Same fix shape as v0.5.381 described, just actually committed this time. Local validation with `bash -eo pipefail`: 183 passed / 0 failed / 4 skipped, exits 0. Lesson: when committing changes that span multiple files, double-check the diff actually contains every hunk before pushing — a forgotten `git stash push` or pre-commit hook can silently drop hunks while the commit message still describes them.

## v0.5.382 — Closes #291: three independent SIGSEGV bug shapes from the same issue, fixed across 4 files. **Bug A** (repros 2 & 3 — `this`-capturing arrow inside a class method): `crates/perry-codegen/src/expr.rs:3319-3329` wrote `0.0` into the reserved `this` capture slot regardless of whether an enclosing `this` was available. The closure body's `Expr::This` then loaded that slot and dereferenced `*(0+0x18)` → SIGSEGV. Fix: load from `ctx.this_stack.last()` when populated; fall back to `0.0` only at module/function level (matches the existing object-literal patch shape at `expr.rs:9234-9253` and the v0.5.377 class-field-init fix, but for arrows in class method bodies). **Bug A inliner companion**: `crates/perry-transform/src/inline.rs::substitute_this` had no `Expr::Closure` arm — fell through `_ => {}` (line 1527), so when `inline_method_call` hoisted a method body to a module-level call site, the inner `Expr::This` inside any nested arrow was never rewritten to `LocalGet(receiver_id)`. After hoisting the closure ran in a frame with no `this_stack` and the codegen-side fix couldn't recover. Added a Closure arm that recurses `substitute_this_in_stmts(body, obj_id)`, clears `captures_this`, and pushes `obj_id` onto the closure's `captures` vec so `compute_auto_captures` includes it deterministically. **Bug B** (repro 1 — `(maybeArr || []).slice().sort(cmp)`): two-stage. (1) `crates/perry-codegen/src/type_analysis.rs::static_type_of` had no arms for `Expr::Logical` or `Expr::Conditional`, so `is_array_expr` returned false for `(source || [])` results. Codegen routed `.slice()` through `js_native_call_method` instead of the dedicated `lower_array_method::"slice"` fast path. Added Logical and Conditional arms that recursively type both branches and union them (mirrors the existing `Expr::IndexGet` arm shape). (2) `crates/perry-runtime/src/object.rs:3210` had `"map"` and `"filter"` arms for arrays in the dispatch tower but no `"slice"` arm. Generic dispatch fell through to `NULL_OBJECT_BYTES` (the static "safe sentinel" placeholder). Downstream `Expr::ArraySort` then fed that pointer to `js_array_sort_with_comparator`; `clean_arr_ptr` rejected it on macOS (placeholder address < `HEAP_MIN = 2 TB`) and returned null; sort returned null; the inline `.length` fast path read `[null - 8]` → SIGSEGV. Added a defensive `"slice"` arm calling `js_array_slice` directly so any path that reaches the runtime dispatcher with an array receiver still gets a real array back. New regression test `test-files/test_issue_291_this_capture_and_slice_chain.ts` (5 sections — Logical fallback + nullish + any-typed Call all chained through slice/sort, class methods with arrow-this in `.map`, generic helper forwarding, multi-method stress with arrow capture) matches `node --experimental-strip-types` byte-for-byte. Verified: cargo build --release clean; `cargo test --release -p perry-runtime --lib` 173/0; `cargo test --release -p perry-codegen --lib` 22/0; gap tests 26/28 = baseline (the 2 failing — `console_methods` / `typed_arrays` — pre-existing categorical/CI gaps unrelated to this change). String concat involving `this.field + arg` inside a `this`-capturing closure is a separate pre-existing type-inference gap (PropertyGet through `this` doesn't propagate the field's String type, so `+` falls into the numeric path and produces `NaN`); deliberately out of scope for this fix.

## v0.5.381 — Tests-workflow fix-up batch on top of v0.5.379 + b2b0a3e6's empty `known_failures.json`. Three independent issues that together held the workflow red: (1) **compile-smoke job exits 1 on success path** (introduced by my v0.5.379 PR #285): the `FAIL=$(ls -1 "$LOGS_DIR"/*.fail 2>/dev/null | wc -l | tr -d ' ')` aggregation in `.github/workflows/test.yml` failed with no matches because GitHub Actions's default `bash -eo pipefail` shell + my added `set -uo pipefail` makes `ls *.fail`'s "no such file" exit 1 propagate through `pipefail` to the outer assignment, then `errexit` kills the script BEFORE the "Compile smoke: X passed..." summary line ever runs. The `xargs -P 6` parallel dispatch and per-test `compile_one` worker were correct; the post-aggregation tripped on a clean run with zero failures. **Fix**: switch all 3 marker counts from `ls | wc -l` pipelines to `shopt -s nullglob` + bash array length (`pass_files=("$LOGS_DIR"/*.pass); PASS=${#pass_files[@]}`). nullglob makes empty globs expand to nothing instead of the literal pattern, so the array length is correctly 0 with no command exiting non-zero. Local validation with `bash -eo pipefail /tmp/extracted_smoke.sh` now exits 0 cleanly: `Compile smoke: 183 passed, 0 failed, 4 skipped`. (2) **doc-tests-macos job fails at `Lint docs/src markdown fences (repo-wide)` step** with 8 untagged ` ```typescript ` fences in `docs/src/plugins/{creating-plugins,overview}.md` (multi-`{{#include}}` blocks + 5 API-signature blocks like `api.setMetadata(...)`) and `docs/src/stdlib/fs.md` (`import { rmRecursive } from "fs";` snippet). The lint at `crates/perry-doc-tests/src/lint.rs::body_is_pure_include` requires fences to be EITHER a single `{{#include}}` directive OR carry `,no-test`. Multi-include fences and bare type signatures fail both criteria. **Fix**: tag each as ` ```typescript,no-test ` since they're API-signature / multi-include blocks that aren't meant to compile-test individually. Verified clean via `cargo run --release --quiet -p perry-doc-tests -- --lint docs/src` → "ok — no untagged typescript fences". (3) **parity job fails because `known_failures.json` is empty `{}`** (b2b0a3e6 cleared it claiming `test_gap_typed_arrays` was fixed, but the test actually still fails on clean main HEAD). Two real bugs need entries: (a) **`test_gap_typed_arrays`** — Uint8ClampedArray index-set doesn't clamp: `c[0]=300; c[1]=-10` reads back `300 -10` instead of `255 0`. b2b0a3e6 added `Uint8ClampedArray` intercepts in `Expr::IndexGet`/`IndexSet` (lines 1687, 2353 of `crates/perry-codegen/src/expr.rs`) routing to `js_typed_array_get`/`js_typed_array_set` (which DO apply ToUint8Clamp via `KIND_UINT8_CLAMPED` in `crates/perry-runtime/src/typedarray.rs::store_at`), but the test's IndexSet path bypasses the intercepts — likely `receiver_class_name` returning None or `lower_index_set_fast` firing first. (b) **`test_issue_154_using_dispose`** — SIGBUS exit 138 silently before any output, pre-existing crash explicitly acknowledged in v0.5.377's CLAUDE.md entry ("reproduces on clean main HEAD pre-fix"). Likely a runtime dispose call dereferencing a bad pointer, or the synthesized `try/finally` from `lower_decl.rs::lower_stmts_using_aware` (v0.5.317) producing a malformed exception frame. Both added to `test-parity/known_failures.json` with `status: "bug"` and detailed reasons including repro commands + investigation pointers + suspected source files so the next worker can find them. PLUS: **fixed a pre-existing JSON-generation quirk in the parity gate** — `run_parity_tests.sh`'s report emits `compile: [""]` when there are zero compile failures (printf+sed quirk), and that empty entry would propagate through the workflow's `Check for new failures` jq pipeline as a literal blank line, then the `comm -23` would report it as a "new failure" (`  - <blank>`) and fail the gate spuriously. Filter via `jq '... | .[] | select(. != "")'` in the workflow. Local simulation of the gate with the new JSON: `GREEN: all 2 failures triaged`. Combined effect: compile-smoke + doc-tests-macos + parity all flip to green; `test_gap_typed_arrays` and `test_issue_154_using_dispose` become tracked-but-not-blocking, ready for the maintainer (or the next worker) to pick up as focused follow-up PRs. cargo-test, build, doc-tests (ubuntu/windows), binary-size were already green on b2b0a3e6.

## v0.5.380 — `perry setup harmonyos` wizard (Phase 1 endgame). Closes the last manual step in the HarmonyOS pipeline that landed across PRs #246-#253: end users now get a one-time interactive setup that probes for DevEco Studio's auto-generated debug signing materials at `~/.ohos/config/`, validates the keystore password via `keytool -list`, auto-extracts the bundle name from the `.p7b` profile's embedded JSON, and persists everything to `~/.perry/config.toml` so subsequent `perry compile --target harmonyos` invocations sign HAPs automatically with no env-var dance. **New `HarmonyosSavedConfig`** in `crates/perry/src/commands/publish.rs` — 5 fields (`p12_path`, `p12_password`, `profile_path`, `cert_path`, `bundle_name`, `key_alias`) wired into `PerryConfig.harmonyos` alongside the existing Apple / Android / Beta entries. **New `harmonyos_wizard()`** in `crates/perry/src/commands/setup.rs` (~180 LOC, mirrors the Android / iOS wizard style): Step 1 probes `~/.ohos/config/` for `default_*.{p12,p7b,cer}` triplets, picks the only one or prompts on multi-keystore installs; Step 2 prompts for the plaintext keystore password (DevEco encrypts this with a machine-bound AES-GCM key in `build-profile.json5` and the decryption isn't externally accessible — wizard documents the workaround of regenerating via DevEco's GUI with a user-chosen password) + verifies it via `keytool -list -storepass`; Step 3 confirms the profile-bound bundle name (auto-extracted by grepping the `.p7b` for `"bundle-name":"..."` since the profile is a PKCS#7 envelope around plaintext-readable JSON). **`crates/perry/src/commands/harmonyos_hap.rs::sign_hap`** rewired so each of the 5 signing inputs falls through env var → saved config; env var still wins when set (per-invocation overrides for CI / multi-cert workflows), saved config kicks in when the env var is absent. The error messages now point users at `perry setup harmonyos` instead of just listing env vars. The setup CLI's `Select` prompt + `match selection` arm + `match platform.as_str()` dispatch all extended to include "HarmonyOS"; `SetupArgs.platform` doc and the unknown-platform `bail!` text both list it. **Verified**: `cargo build --release -p perry` clean from the worktree; `harmonyos_wizard` is the 7th platform wizard so the existing test surface (Android / iOS / visionOS / macOS / tvOS / watchOS / Windows) extends transparently. **End-to-end on the user's actual DevEco Studio 6.0.2 + Pura 90 Pro Max emulator** is the next step — once the user runs `perry setup harmonyos` and pastes their regenerated debug-cert password, `perry compile foo.ts --target harmonyos -o /tmp/libfoo.so && hdc install /tmp/libfoo.hap` should succeed end-to-end.

## v0.5.379 — CI hygiene (Tests workflow audit, batch 1 of 2). Bumped above origin's parallel-track v0.5.378 (#286 — plugins/canvas docs fence conversion) per the merge-collision precedent. Two zero-risk wins surfaced by the timing audit on run #25095693388 (build 6m25s + cargo-test 4m36s + parity 16m20s + compile-smoke 26m24s + 3× doc-tests 28-40m, ~950 multiplier-min/run, ~84% on macos-14). (1) **`run_parity_tests.sh:218`** — the per-test compile invocation was `cargo run --quiet --bin perry --` with no `--release`, which silently triggered a *debug* build of perry as a side effect of `cargo run`'s default profile. The prior step `cargo build --release` produced `target/release/perry` but the loop never used it; instead cargo built a parallel `target/debug/perry` on the first iteration and reused that for the remaining ~150 tests, paying both the cold debug-compile cost (~2-3 min) and the slower-runtime debug binary per test. Fix: explicit `PERRY_BIN="$SCRIPT_DIR/target/release/perry"`, build via `cargo build --release --quiet -p perry -p perry-runtime -p perry-stdlib`, and call `"$PERRY_BIN" $BACKEND_FLAG "$test_file" -o "$perry_binary"` directly per test — skips cargo's per-call overhead × 150 entirely. Expected savings: 2-4 min off the parity job. (2) **`.github/workflows/test.yml::compile-smoke`** — the `for f in test-files/*.ts; do "$PERRY" "$f" -o ...; done` loop was strictly sequential at ~12s / file × ~130 files = 26 min wall. Refactored to a `compile_one()` worker function dispatched via `printf '%s\n' test-files/*.ts | xargs -P "${PERRY_SMOKE_JOBS:-6}" -n 1 -I{} bash -c 'compile_one "$@"' _ {}`. Per-file `.pass` / `.fail` / `.skip` marker writes under `$LOGS_DIR` are race-free (each test owns a unique marker filename), so concurrent workers never collide; PASS/FAIL/SKIP counts and the failure list are aggregated AFTER `xargs` returns by counting markers + iterating `*.fail`. The skip-list / stderr-capture / "head 30 lines of failing log directly in job output" affordances are all preserved. Bash 3.2 compat preserved (macOS-14 ships /bin/bash 3.2, no associative arrays, no `wait -n`). Default `NJOBS=6` chosen as ~2× the macos-14 runner's 3 vCPUs to overlap clang link I/O with codegen CPU; `PERRY_SMOKE_JOBS` env override added for future runner spec changes. **Local validation**: 2m 21s for 187 files (16× speedup over sequential extrapolation, 6 different `target/perry-auto-*` build dirs created, 304% CPU avg = 3 cores busy after the cargo lockfile serializes auto-optimize rebuilds). On CI's 3-vCPU macos-14 expect ~3-4× speedup → 26 min → ~6-8 min. Combined wall-clock impact: Tests workflow ~40 min → ~22 min, ~950 → ~700 multiplier-min/run. **Out of scope** (audit deliverable, separate follow-up PRs): drop the unused `build` job (its artifacts aren't downloaded by anyone), move parity / compile-smoke / cargo-test off macos-14 to ubuntu-latest (10× billing-weight cut), adopt `Swatinem/rust-cache@v2` workspace-wide, consolidate xcompile-only doc-tests to one Linux job, `paths-ignore: ['docs/src/**', '**.md']` to skip Tests on doc-only PRs.

## v0.5.378 — v0.5.376 docs follow-up: convert the plugins + canvas snippet fences from `text` → verified `{{#include}}` extracts. New `docs/examples/ui/canvas/snippets.ts` (6 anchors: `imports`, `create`, `rectangles`, `lines`, `arcs`, `text`) — `run: false` per the canvas-needs-run-loop convention. New `docs/examples/plugins/host_snippets.ts` (8 anchors covering the 12-fn `PERRY_PLUGIN_TABLE`: `imports`, `init`, `load`, `discover`, `introspect`, `emit-hook`, `emit-event`, `invoke-tool`, `unload`).
