GTK4 at 39/43 (4 remaining Missing are unrelated splitview / tabbar / qrcode rows that aren't styling-prop rows but slipped in during Phase A categorization), Windows at 38/43 + 5 Stub (the deferred-paint family), Web at 6/43 (CSS column tracked separately).

## v0.5.300 — Issue #185 Phase B closures 7+8+9: opacity + borders + text decoration. Three closures landing together because they all close the same shape (the GTK4 / Windows / Web cells the v0.5.297 shadow closure left Missing) plus add a brand-new aspirational row. **B7 opacity** (`perry_ui_widget_set_opacity`): GTK4 wired via built-in `Widget::set_opacity` (single-line passthrough — no CSS provider needed). Windows is stub-with-state — `OPACITY_VALUES: Mutex<Vec<(i64, f64)>>` mirrors the existing `CORNER_RADII` deferred-application pattern; real per-widget opacity needs `WS_EX_LAYERED` + `SetLayeredWindowAttributes` per-class wiring. Web aliased to the existing `perry_ui_set_opacity` JS function via the WASM emitter dispatch table — `"setOpacity" | "set_opacity" | "widgetSetOpacity"` all route to the same symbol; no new JS code. Matrix opacity row goes from `[Wired×6, Missing×3]` to `[Wired×7, Stub_Windows, Wired_Web]`. **B8 borders** (`perry_ui_widget_set_border_color` + `perry_ui_widget_set_border_width`): joint per-handle (color, width) state on every backend because CSS won't render a border unless `border-style: solid` + a non-zero width + a color all land in the same rule — calling either setter alone with naive cascading would clobber the other. GTK4 uses thread-local `BORDER_STATE: HashMap<i64, (Option<color>, Option<width>)>` + a regenerated per-handle `perry-bd-{h}` CSS class with `CssProvider` re-emitted on every change; mirrors the v0.5.297 shadow `perry-sh-{h}` pattern. Web adds two new JS functions `perry_ui_widget_set_border_color` / `perry_ui_widget_set_border_width` backed by a module-level `__perryBorderState` Map and a `__perry_apply_border` helper that reads color + width together and writes `el.style.border = \`${w}px solid rgba(R,G,B,a)\``. Defaults match CALayer-ish behavior: missing color = black, missing width = 1px so calling either setter alone still produces a visible border. Windows is stub-with-state with joint `BORDER_STATE: Mutex<Vec<(i64, (Option<color>, Option<width>))>>`. Matrix flips both border rows from `[Wired×6, Missing×3]` to `[Wired×7, Stub_Windows, Wired_Web]`. **B9 text decoration** (`perry_ui_text_set_decoration` — new aspirational row from Phase A flipped to live): values `0=none, 1=underline, 2=strikethrough` map to each backend's native mechanism. Apple (macOS / iOS / tvOS / visionOS) build an `NSAttributedString` via `[NSDictionary dictionaryWithObject:numberWithInt:1 forKey:@"NSUnderline"]` (or `@"NSStrikethrough"`) + `[NSAttributedString alloc] initWithString:attributes:` then `setAttributedStringValue:` (NSTextField) or `setAttributedText:` (UILabel); `decoration = 0` resets back to plain `setStringValue:` / `setText:`. Pattern mirrors the existing `button::set_text_color` raw-pointer JNI bridge so the objc2 trait bounds compose. watchOS adds a `text_decoration: i64` field to `NodeData` for the SwiftUI host to consume. Android calls `View.getPaint().setFlags(8|16)` (`Paint.UNDERLINE_TEXT_FLAG`=8, `Paint.STRIKE_THRU_TEXT_FLAG`=16) + `View.invalidate()` over JNI — simpler than building a `SpannableString` and gives the same visual result. GTK4 uses `pango::AttrInt::new_underline(Single|None)` + `new_strikethrough(bool)` inserted into the existing `Label::attributes()` AttrList. Web emits `el.style.textDecoration = "underline" | "line-through" | "none"`. Windows is stub-with-state — `DECORATION_VALUES: Mutex<Vec<(i64, i64)>>` stores the value but rebuilding the HFONT with `lfUnderline`/`lfStrikeOut` set requires `GetObjectW` + LOGFONT mod + `CreateFontIndirectW` + `WM_SETFONT`, deferred. Matrix flips the `decoration` row from all-Missing baseline to `[Wired×7, Stub_Windows, Wired_Web]`. **Codegen + TS surface**: new `textSetDecoration` row in `crates/perry-codegen/src/lower_call.rs::NATIVE_MODULE_TABLE` with `[Widget, I64Raw]` arg kinds; new TS export `textSetDecoration(widget, decoration)` in `types/perry/ui/index.d.ts`; `widgetSetBorderColor` / `widgetSetBorderWidth` get explicit Web aliases in `crates/perry-codegen-wasm/src/emit.rs` so user code calling them resolves to the new JS functions on the web target. **Matrix summary** post-landing: every Apple platform + Android at **42/43 Wired** (1 remaining gap = `hidden`, pre-existing audit miss), GTK4 at 38/43 (5 remaining unrelated Missing — splitview, tabbar etc.), Windows at 38/43 + 5 Stub (shadow + opacity + border_color + border_width + text decoration — the deferred-paint family), Web at 5/43 (CSS columns intentionally tracked separately). Drift integration test still clean across all 8 native platforms.

## v0.5.298 — Issue #188: wire codegen dispatch for `perry/i18n` format wrappers. New `PERRY_I18N_TABLE` in `crates/perry-codegen/src/lower_call.rs` routes `Currency`/`Percent`/`FormatNumber`/`ShortDate`/`LongDate`/`FormatTime`/`Raw` to per-name `perry_i18n_format_*_default` runtime exports added in `crates/perry-runtime/src/i18n.rs` (single-arg shape — each wrapper folds in `LOCALE_INDEX` so codegen stays uniform). New `UiReturnKind::Str` variant returns the runtime's `*mut StringHeader` NaN-boxed with `STRING_TAG`. Pre-fix, `Currency(99.99)` reached the receiver-less early-out at `lower_call.rs:2849` and returned NaN-boxed `undefined`; now it returns `"$99.99"`. Doc snippet `docs/examples/i18n/format_wrappers.ts` + golden stdout added to keep the wiring drift-checked. (Pre-existing FP-precision quirk in `format_number_locale` — `1234567.89` → `1,234,567.8899999999` — unchanged; that's formatter math, separate from dispatch.)

## v0.5.297 — Issue #185 Phases A + B (consolidated landing): perry/ui styling audit infrastructure + cross-platform `widgetSetShadow`. **Phase A** — new `crates/perry-ui/src/styling_matrix.rs` declarative matrix (43 styling-relevant FFI rows × 9 platforms macOS/iOS/tvOS/visionOS/watchOS/Android/GTK4/Windows/Web, each cell `Status::{Wired,Stub,Missing,NotApplicable}`); machine-derived initial state by scanning each backend's `lib.rs` exports — caught two prior-doc errors (the older `perry-ui-test::FEATURES` table claimed Apple platforms + Android lacked CALayer borders + opacity entirely, while reality is that GTK4 + Windows are the actual gaps). Drift-check binary `crates/perry-ui/src/bin/styling-matrix.rs` (`--check`/`--gen`/`--diff` modes) handles both multi-line and single-line `#[no_mangle] pub extern "C" fn ...` declarations (watchOS uses single-line). Integration test `crates/perry-ui/tests/styling_matrix_drift.rs` makes drift fail `cargo test --workspace`. `scripts/run_ui_styling_matrix.sh` + `.github/workflows/test.yml` step with `git diff --exit-code` guard so a forgotten `--gen` regen also fails CI. Auto-generated `docs/src/ui/styling-matrix.md`. Sibling `perry-ui-test::FEATURES` left untouched — consolidation deferred to Phase C. **Phase B** — `widgetSetShadow(handle, r, g, b, a, blur, offset_x, offset_y)` wired across all 9 platforms in 5 closures: (1) macOS / iOS / tvOS / visionOS via CALayer.shadow* (`setShadowColor:` opaque + `setShadowOpacity:` so non-1 alpha doesn't double-multiply, `setShadowRadius:` for blur, `setShadowOffset:` as CGSize where +y = downward to match HTML `box-shadow`, `setMasksToBounds: NO` so corner-radius widgets don't clip the shadow). (2) watchOS stores shadow in the `NodeData` introspection tree (new `shadow: Option<(f64,f64,f64,f64,f64,f64,f64)>` field + initializer) so the SwiftUI host can apply `.shadow(...)` modifier. (3) Web via CSS `box-shadow` in `crates/perry-codegen-wasm/src/wasm_runtime.js` — emits `el.style.boxShadow = \`${dx}px ${dy}px ${blur}px rgba(R,G,B,a)\`` with a dispatch-table row in `emit.rs` plus three runtime dynamic-dispatch maps registered + the export list updated. (4) GTK4 via per-handle CSS class `perry-sh-{h}` + fresh `CssProvider` emitting `box-shadow: <dx>px <dy>px <blur>px rgba(R,G,B,a);`, mirroring `set_corner_radius`'s display-priority pattern for buttons + widget-priority for others. (5) Android via Material `setElevation(blur/2 dp)` over JNI + opportunistic `setOutlineSpotShadowColor`/`setOutlineAmbientShadowColor` for color tinting on API 28+ (silent no-op on older API). Offset is intentionally ignored on Android — the device-level light source owns shadow direction. (6) Windows is **stub-with-state**: `static SHADOW_PARAMS: Mutex<Vec<(i64, ShadowData)>>` mirrors the existing `CORNER_RADII` deferred-application pattern; FFI symbol resolves and parameters are stored, but real DirectComposition / WM_PAINT alpha-blit rendering deferred to a follow-up. Matrix marks Windows `Status::Stub` (not `Wired`) so users know the prop is honored but not visible. Cross-platform code that calls `widgetSetShadow` compiles + links + matrix-drift-checks clean on every backend; when the Windows paint pass lands, every previously-stored handle gets its shadow applied automatically. New codegen dispatch row in `crates/perry-codegen/src/lower_call.rs::NATIVE_MODULE_TABLE` routes `widget.setShadow(...)` to `perry_ui_widget_set_shadow` with `[Widget, F64×7]` arg kinds. New TS export `widgetSetShadow` in `types/perry/ui/index.d.ts`. End-to-end smoke: `./perry compile docs/examples/ui/styling/shadow.ts` produces a 0.9 MB macOS binary; `--target web` produces a 179 KB self-contained HTML with the boxShadow CSS exactly where expected (5 occurrences of `perry_ui_widget_set_shadow` in the emitted HTML, matching `perry_ui_set_corner_radius`'s reference count). Matrix shadow row goes from all-Missing baseline to `[Wired×5_Apple, Wired_Android, Wired_GTK4, Stub_Windows, Wired_Web]` — every cell non-Missing for the first time. Per-platform Wired summary post-shadow: 41/43 Apple platforms + Android, 38/43 + 1 stub Windows, 34/43 GTK4 (still has 9 missing — borders, opacity, etc., from earlier audit gaps that are Phase B's remaining work), 1/43 Web (Web column intentionally tracked separately as it uses CSS string emission rather than FFI). Restoration note: this commit consolidates the v0.5.295/296/297/298 work that was lost in a stash/rebase race against the v0.5.296 FUNDING.yml commit; `git fsck` recovered the 6 new files from `stash@{0}^3` (the untracked-files component of `pre-rebase stash for v0.5.300 push`) and the Phase B FFI deltas were restored from `stash@{0}` proper, leaving an orthogonal docs-drift stash unmerged for separate review.

## v0.5.294 — Release-blocker fix surfaced by v0.5.293's failed publish: `_js_stdlib_process_pending` link error on macOS doc-tests + iOS simulator tests. Root cause was Cargo feature unification — when CI's auto-optimize runs `cargo build -p perry-runtime -p perry-stdlib` together, perry-stdlib's `Cargo.toml` declares `perry-runtime = { features = ["stdlib"] }`, which activates `stdlib` on perry-runtime. That activates the `#[cfg(not(feature = "stdlib"))]` gate at `crates/perry-runtime/src/lib.rs:65` and excludes `mod stdlib_stubs;`, removing `_js_stdlib_process_pending` from `libperry_runtime.a`. Perry's compile then enters runtime-only link mode (libperry_runtime.a + libperry_ui_macos.a, no libperry_stdlib.a) and the symbol is undefined. Local builds didn't catch it because `cargo build -p perry-runtime` alone doesn't unify with stdlib's feature requirements. Fix: 18 files across `perry-ui-{macos,ios,tvos,visionos,gtk4}` switched from hard-linking `js_stdlib_process_pending` to calling `js_run_stdlib_pump`, the existing always-exported trampoline at `lib.rs:121` that dispatches via the registered-callback pattern (same shape `js_stdlib_has_active_handles` already uses). Also re-added `test_gap_console_methods` to `test-parity/known_failures.json` as `ci-env` — the v0.5.290 drop was premature; it passes locally through `normalize_output` but the CI runner produces a variant that escapes it. Re-tagging for `release-packages.yml` since v0.5.293's GH release shipped no binaries.

## v0.5.293 — Repo hygiene: untrack 465 Android Gradle cache files (`android-build/.gradle/`, `android-build/app/build/`, `android-build/build/`) that were churning on every Gradle invocation, and add the matching `.gitignore` rules. Also gitignored: `docs/examples/_reports/` (CI-generated doc-test report), `/assets/` + `benchmarks/suite/assets/` (external game-project assets the user keeps adjacent for perry-ui-* manual testing — never source), and stray repro binaries `enum_repro`/`no_pragma_test`. Bench methodology: `json_polyglot/run.sh` precompiles Node TS to `.mjs` (esbuild → npx-esbuild → tsc fallback chain) as untimed setup so Node isn't charged for `--experimental-strip-types`'s per-launch parse on every run — Perry is AOT and Bun strips natively, so neither pays this; falls back to the old `--experimental-strip-types` invocation with a banner if no stripper is available. `polyglot/bench.rs` gains an FP-contract caveat block on `bench_loop_data_dependent` documenting the FMA-contract (Apple Clang, Go) vs no-contract (Rust, Swift, Perry, Node, Bun, Java) clustering. Plus `tests/test_array_index_loop.sh` runner companion to the existing `.ts` regression test.

## v0.5.290 — Stub audit: `test_gap_console_methods` removed from `known_failures.json` — passes through the parity-runner's `normalize_output` despite the raw diff showing different timer values. The test's only divergence is `console.time` measurements (Perry's compiled native code is faster than Node's interpreter, so e.g. `timer1: 3.888ms` (Node) vs `timer1: 0.002ms` (Perry)). The parity runner has had a `s/^([^:]+): [0-9]+(\.[0-9]+)?(ms|s)$/\1: <timer>/g` substitution since v0.5.181 (issue #155 fix) for exactly this case; the entry was just stale documentation post that. Verified empty diff under parity-runner-style normalization across both stdout and stderr. Net `known_failures.json` reduction: 16 → 15. No code change.

## v0.5.289 — CI hygiene: stop the `Tests` workflow's macos-14 jobs from OOM'ing on disk space. Recent runs (24938059592, 24936703670, 24935828472, ...) failed at the cache-restore step with `System.IO.IOException: No space left on device` from the GitHub Runner's own diagnostic writer — the worker died before cargo started, no useful logs. Two coordinated changes in `.github/workflows/test.yml`: (1) **dropped `target/` from the cargo cache paths** in all 5 cache blocks (`build`, `cargo-test`, `parity`, `compile-smoke`, `doc-tests` matrix) — kept `~/.cargo/registry` + `~/.cargo/git` (small, gives ~80% of the warm-build win). The accumulated release-mode `target/` was the load-bearing source of disk pressure; restoring it before the build started had pushed usage past the macos-14 runner's ~14 GB free-disk floor. Inline note in each `path:` block explains why `target/` is intentionally excluded so a future cleanup doesn't add it back. (2) **added a "Free up disk space (macOS)" step** right after `actions/checkout@v4` in each of the 5 jobs, gated on `if: runner.os == 'macOS'` so the same insertion is safe in the doc-tests matrix (Ubuntu/Windows legs no-op). Wipes `/Library/Developer/CoreSimulator/Profiles/Runtimes/*Simulator*` (the iOS/tvOS/watchOS simulator runtime IMAGES — not the SDKs) and `~/Library/Developer/CoreSimulator/Caches/*`. Reclaims ~15-25 GB without affecting cross-compilation to `aarch64-apple-ios-sim` (the `-ios` doc-tests pre-build only needs the SDK, which lives inside the active Xcode app). Step prints `Disk free: BEFORE -> AFTER` for visibility. `release-packages.yml` deliberately untouched — its macos-14/macos-15 matrix legs don't cache `target/` and last release run (v0.5.178) succeeded; will revisit if it starts failing. YAML-validated via `python3 -c "import yaml; yaml.safe_load(...)"`. Pure CI change; no code, no test, no rebuild required.

## v0.5.288 — Stub audit: `test_json` removed from `known_failures.json`, incidentally fixed by v0.5.286's `JSON.stringify(<plain f64>)` segfault fix. The test exercises `JSON.stringify(42)` / `JSON.stringify(3.14)` etc. directly, so the same too-loose raw-pointer check in `try_stringify_lazy_array` was crashing it on the first `console.log(JSON.stringify(<num>))`; with that branch tightened to `top16 == 0`, the test now matches Node byte-for-byte (verified across 2 isolated runs). Same one-line fix; no new code change needed. Net `known_failures.json` reduction: 16 → 15. perry-runtime tests 168/168.

## v0.5.286 — Stub audit: `JSON.stringify(<plain f64>)` segfaulted. `try_stringify_lazy_array` in `crates/perry-runtime/src/json.rs:2350` had a too-loose raw-pointer heuristic at line 2355 — `} else if top16 < 0x7FF8 {` accepted ANY f64 whose upper 16 bits were below the NaN-tag band, including regular numbers like `42.0` (top16=`0x4045`). It then computed `gc_header = bits - GC_HEADER_SIZE` and dereferenced `0x4045_0000_0000_0000 - 8 = 0x4044_FFFF_FFFF_FFF8` as a `*const GcHeader`, segfaulting on `(*gc_header).obj_type`. Match the `EXC_BAD_ACCESS address=0x4044fffffffffff8` from `lldb` exactly. Fix: tighten the raw-pointer check to `top16 == 0` (real heap pointers on 64-bit systems fit in the lower 48 bits, so genuine raw pointers have zero upper-16; numbers, NaN-box tags, and other non-pointer values all have non-zero upper-16). Same heuristic in the sibling `redirect_lazy_to_materialized` at line 2310 was already correct (only handles `top16 == 0x7FFD`); no change needed there. Verified: `JSON.stringify(42)` now prints `42` (was: SIGSEGV); `test_edge_json_regex` matches Node byte-for-byte across 68 lines (was: zero output, exit 139 on the first `console.log(JSON.stringify(42))`). Removed from `known_failures.json` (15 entries remaining). perry-runtime tests 168/168, lazy-JSON sanity sweep clean (test_json_typed_basic / test_json_lazy_indexed / test_edge_buffer_from_encoding / test_super_calls).

## v0.5.285 — Bench docs prose pass on `benchmarks/README.md`. Three small consistency fixes, no numbers/tables/code touched. (1) §4 Strengths first bullet (JSON validate-and-roundtrip): replaced "3.5× over Bun (259 ms), 5.3× over Node (394 ms), 6.0× over Kotlin server JIT (453 ms)" with bare times ("Bun 259 ms, Node 394 ms, Kotlin server JIT 453 ms") — multipliers read as marketing copy that the rest of the page has been disciplined about avoiding; the times alone make the same point with lower temperature and don't risk being screenshotted out of context. (2) §2 Optimized-flags Go bullet: rewrote "Go cannot close the gap at all: no `-ffast-math`, no `reassoc` flag, the Go compiler doesn't ship that pipeline" to scope the limitation to optimization-probe kernels and explicitly cross-reference `loop_data_dependent` (where Go wins via FMA fusion) — as written, the absolute claim contradicted the TL;DR's own loop_data_dependent finding. (3) §1 Honest-disclaimers Go bullet: trimmed the trailing compute-table sentence ("Go has no `-ffast-math` flag; `accumulate` and `loop_overhead` deltas in the compute table are unrecoverable in stock Go") since after fix (2), §2's Go bullet is the canonical place for that claim — §1 is the JSON disclaimers section, doesn't belong there. Pure prose; no tests, no code, no benchmark rerun.

## v0.5.284 — Stub audit: two correctness bugs in the Promise microtask runner. (1) **Microtask order was LIFO instead of FIFO.** `TASK_QUEUE` in `crates/perry-runtime/src/promise.rs:53` was a `Vec<...>` and the runner at line 326 popped via `.pop()` (from the END) — so `Promise.resolve(1).then(a)` and `Promise.resolve(2).then(b)` registered in source order ran their continuations in REVERSE order (b then a). Visible symptom: `test_stress_promises` printed every later `console.log` BEFORE every earlier one. Fix: switched the queue to `VecDeque` and the pop to `.pop_front()`; updated all four `.push(...)` sites to `.push_back(...)` (the `SCHEDULED_RESOLVES` queue at line 636 is a separate structure, untouched). (2) **Throws inside `.then(handler)` / `.catch(handler)` body crashed the program instead of rejecting the next promise.** The microtask runner at `js_promise_run_microtasks` called `js_closure_call1(callback, value)` directly — the closure body's `js_throw` then longjmp'd to whatever setjmp was active, but `TRY_DEPTH == 0` at that point so `js_throw` hit the `print_uncaught(value); std::process::exit(1)` arm at exception.rs:84-85. Fix: wrap the closure call in setjmp via the same Rust→`extern "C" fn setjmp` pattern `gc.rs::mark_stack_roots:1378` already uses; on longjmp-return retrieve the exception via `js_get_exception` / clear it / pop the try block, and reject the next promise with the exception value. Also moved the null-callback pass-through fast path out of the call branch so a null `on_fulfilled` propagates the value (vs being treated as fulfilled-with-no-callback) and a null `on_rejected` propagates the rejection (the previous code resolved next with the reason — wrong direction). Verified: 3-promise FIFO + rethrown-rejection minimal repros now match Node byte-for-byte. perry-runtime tests 168/168, sanity sweep on test_async2 / test_super_calls / test_edge_buffer_from_encoding all pass. **Not removed from `known_failures.json`**: `test_stress_promises` still fails on four other distinct issues — `new Promise<T>((resolve, reject) => ...)` constructor body not running, `Promise.any` produces no output, `.then(p => Promise.resolve(...))` doesn't unwrap inner Promise (logs `Promise { <pending> }`), `.finally(() => ...).then(v => ...)` value-passing wrong. Each one is a focused dive of its own; reason field updated to enumerate them.

## v0.5.283 — Bench docs: rewrote the f64 bullet in `benchmarks/README.md` §Strengths so it doesn't carry contradictory framing. Pre-fix, the bullet claimed "Perry 3-8× faster than native compilers' default release builds" while in the same sentence saying those benchmarks "measure compiler optimization aggressiveness, not runtime performance" — the strain was visible to readers and the headline number was being put in the section that's supposed to make only unambiguous claims. New bullet leads on the defensible part: Perry's release-mode defaults emit `reassoc contract` fast-math flags (the minimum IEEE deviations TypeScript's `number` type can't observe — no signalling NaNs, no fenv, no operator-level `-0`) so LLVM's IndVarSimplify + autovectorizer fire on trivially-foldable accumulators where strict-IEEE languages need explicit `-ffast-math` / `-ffp-contract=fast` / `fadd_fast`; on the genuinely-non-foldable `loop_data_dependent` kernel Perry lands at **235 ms median** dead-on the no-contract compiled-pack cluster (Rust 229, Swift 233, Java 229, Bun 232; FMA-contract pack at 128 ms wins by FMUL+FADD→FMADDD fusion, which LLVM matches under `-ffp-contract=fast`); the larger gaps Perry shows on `loop_overhead` / `math_intensive` / `accumulate` are *because those kernels are foldable* and Perry's defaults let the optimizer fold them — `clang++ -O3 -ffast-math` closes those gaps to within a millisecond. The "3-8× faster than native" framing is now confined to the Optimization-probes subsection where it's already correctly framed as flag-aggressiveness probing not runtime perf. Also: Optimization-probes "These four cells" → "These five cells" (table actually has 5 rows since v0.5.271 added the loop_data_dependent companion); inline reference to the probes subsection from the new Strengths bullet now correctly says "above" instead of "below" (subsection lives in TL;DR §Compute, Strengths is §4, file ordering puts probes above). **Compute microbench captions corrected**: TL;DR §Compute caption was missing the run date; §2 caption was actively wrong — claimed "Existing run, last refreshed 2026-04-22 at v0.5.164 — predates the RUNS=11 methodology change" but `polyglot/RESULTS_AUTO.md` actually says `Runs per cell: 11 · Date: 2026-04-25 · Perry version: v0.5.249` (the existing wording was load-bearing for one of Prompt 3's acceptance criteria — "data was collected and under which methodology" needed to actually be true). Both captions now accurately say "RUNS=11 medians from a fresh 2026-04-25 polyglot run at v0.5.249" and note that v0.5.249→v0.5.282 commits are JSON-runtime fixes (NaN equality, SSO consumers, ECMAScript number formatting) that don't touch the codegen paths these benches exercise — so a rerun is on the follow-up list but the gap is at the noise floor. **Compiler-versions table refreshed** (was outdated): rustc 1.85→1.94.1 (verified `rustc --version` on this machine), Apple clang 17→21.0.0, Swift 6.0→6.3.1, Java→OpenJDK 21.0.7, Node v20→v25.8.0, Bun 1.3→1.3.12, Python 3.12→CPython 3.14.3. **`benchmarks/polyglot/METHODOLOGY.md` brought current and de-stale-d**: header dated 2026-04-15 (pre v0.5.22) → 2026-04-25 with v0.5.281; suite description "Eight compute-bound microbenchmarks" → nine (loop_data_dependent landed v0.5.271); methodology line "Best of 5 runs ... is reported" → "RUNS=11 ... median + p95 + σ + min + max" (the RUNS=11 rollout from v0.5.243 era was already in the Statistics subsection but the top-of-doc summary still claimed best-of-5); compiler-versions table refreshed to actually-installed; iteration-count table extended with the loop_data_dependent row (`100M iters, 64-element x[], sum = sum*x[i%64] + x[(i*7)%64] on [0.5, 1.0)`). **New top-level section `loop_data_dependent — what happens when the compiler can't fold`** with kernel design (multiplicative carry resists autovectorization, runtime-loaded array indices block LICM), asm-level analysis (rustc -O and clang++ -O3 both emit `LDR, LDR, FMUL, FADD` 4-instruction loop, ~6-8 cycle dependency chain on M1's FP unit), the two FP-contract clusters explanation (FMA pack 128 ms via FMADDD fusion = 3-instruction loop, 4-cycle chain; no-contract pack 229-235 ms with separate FMUL+FADD), Why-Go-is-in-the-FMA-pack resolution (`cmd/compile/internal/ssa/fmaArm64.go` since Go 1.14 + Apple Clang's lower fusion threshold than mainline LLVM — flag-default story not "Go is fundamentally faster"), Node 322 ms outlier explanation (JIT-warmup / OS-scheduler this-run anomaly with σ=63, p95=447, min=259), and an explicit "what this benchmark answers" wrap-up that names the headline claim "Perry is 7× faster than C++ on `loop_overhead` does not generalize to all f64 compute". Also: new top-level `Optimization probes` section in METHODOLOGY consistent with the README's framing so a reader landing on METHODOLOGY directly gets the same probe-vs-runtime-perf framing as a reader landing on README. Changelog entry added for the 2026-04-25 v0.5.249→v0.5.282 refresh. **Verified runner output format matches README claim**: both `polyglot/run_all.sh` and `json_polyglot/run.sh` invoke a shared-shape `compute_stats` awk routine that emits `median|p95|stddev|min|max` per cell into RESULTS_AUTO.md (`## Per-cell full stats` section) — the README's Reproducing-section claim that `./run.sh` emits "median + p95 + σ + min + max" is accurate; no runner change needed. Pure docs commit; no code, no test, no codegen change. CHANGELOG.md not touched (entry consolidated here).

## v0.5.281 — Stub audit: two distinct bugs in the NaN/number-formatting family. (1) **`NaN == NaN` returned `true` in Perry but `false` in Node** (IEEE 754: NaN compares unequal to itself; spec calls for the same in JS `==`). Root cause: `js_loose_eq` in `crates/perry-runtime/src/builtins.rs:850` had a `if a.bits() == b.bits() { return true; }` fast-path BEFORE the number-IEEE check at line 864, so two `f64::NAN` operands with identical bits hit the fast path and returned true. Fix: reorder so `is_number && is_number` is checked FIRST and routes through IEEE 754 equality (which correctly returns false for NaN==NaN AND true for +0==-0). The bit-equality fast path stays for non-numeric same-bits cases (null==null, identical pointers, identical SSO encodings). Strict `===` was already correct because the codegen path for two Number-typed operands uses `fcmp oeq` (which returns false for NaN) — only `==` was broken. (2) **`Number.MAX_VALUE` printed as 309 zeros and `Number.EPSILON` as 16-leading-zero decimal** instead of Node's scientific-notation `1.7976931348623157e+308` / `2.220446049250313e-16`. Five number-formatting sites in the runtime emitted `format!("{}", value)` for non-integer floats, which uses Rust's Display impl (full decimal regardless of magnitude) instead of ECMAScript NumberToString (scientific when `|n| >= 10^21` or `|n| < 10^-6`). Fix: extract a `format_finite_number_js` helper at `builtins.rs` top, call it from all 5 float-format sites (`js_console_log_number`, `js_console_log_dynamic`'s number branch, `js_console_error_number`, `js_console_error_dynamic`, `js_console_warn_number`, `js_console_warn_dynamic`, plus `format_jsvalue` used by spread/multi-arg console.log and util.inspect). Helper applies the threshold split: `abs >= 1e21 || abs < 1e-6 → fix_exponent_format(format!("{:e}", value))`, else `format!("{}", value)`. `fix_exponent_format` is the existing `string.rs` helper that converts Rust's `1.23e308` to JS's `1.23e+308`; promoted from private to `pub(crate)` so builtins.rs can reuse it. Same threshold logic also added to `js_number_to_string` and `format_number_for_js` in `string.rs` (the toString / toPrecision-with-precision-0 paths). Verified: `console.log(Number.MAX_VALUE)` prints `1.7976931348623157e+308`, `console.log(Number.EPSILON)` prints `2.220446049250313e-16`, `console.log(1e-6)` stays decimal at `0.000001`, `console.log(1e-7)` switches to `1e-7`. test_stress_nanbox matches Node byte-for-byte (was diverging on both NaN equality and number formatting). Removed from `known_failures.json` (now 16 entries). perry-runtime tests 168/168.

## v0.5.280 — Stub audit: NaN/Infinity ToInt32 coercion. `is_known_finite` in `crates/perry-codegen/src/expr.rs:8272` accepted any `Expr::Number(_)` literal as "finite" — including `Number(f64::NAN)` and `Number(f64::INFINITY)` (the HIR's representation of the `NaN` and `Infinity` global identifiers per `lower.rs:4956-4961`). The `BitOr-with-0` fast-path then routed `(NaN) | 0` through `toint32_fast` (which skips the NaN/Inf guard, assuming the operand is finite), emitting raw `fptosi NaN to i32` — which is **poison** in LLVM — followed by `or i32 poison, 0` → poison → `sitofp poison to double`. LLVM constant-folded the chain to a value whose bit pattern coincidentally matched `STRING_TAG | <some-pointer>`, which downstream consumers (console.log dynamic-dispatch in particular) interpreted as a NaN-boxed string handle. Visible symptom on the issue's repro: `console.log("(NaN) | 0:", (NaN) | 0)` printed `(NaN) | 0: (NaN) | 0:` (label twice, value missing) because the second arg was being decoded as the "(NaN) | 0:" string literal. Fix: split the existing `Expr::Integer(_) | Expr::Number(_) => true` arm so that `Expr::Number(n)` returns `n.is_finite()` — `Integer` is always finite by construction; `Number` may not be. Verified: `(NaN) | 0`, `(Infinity) | 0`, `(-Infinity) | 0` all now correctly return `0` per ECMAScript ToInt32 (was: poison-derived garbage). Pre-existing `let x = NaN; x | 0` path (which goes through the safe `toint32` because LocalGet-of-Number-typed-local is conservatively NOT in `integer_locals`) was already correct and remains so. perry-runtime tests 168/168. **Not removed from `known_failures.json`**: `test_stress_int_ops` still diverges from Node on `console.log(numberArray)` formatting — Node's util.inspect right-aligns integer-array elements to common width and computes per-line count from terminal width, Perry packs without padding 4-per-line. That's a util.inspect feature, not a correctness bug; reason field updated to capture both the now-fixed NaN coercion and the remaining formatting gap.

## v0.5.279 — #187 follow-up (stub audit): SSO + property-read NaN bug. `JSON.parse('{"foo":"perry"}').foo` rendered as `NaN` even though `typeof a.foo === 'string'` and `Object.keys(a)` showed the key, and `JSON.parse(...).foo === "perry"` returned `false`. Root cause: every printer / formatter / equality consumer in `crates/perry-runtime/src/builtins.rs` and `value.rs` was using `JSValue::is_string()` (which only matches heap `STRING_TAG = 0x7FFF`) where it should have used `is_any_string()` (which also matches inline `SHORT_STRING_TAG = 0x7FF9`, the SSO tag landed in v0.5.213-216). Since v0.5.216, `DirectParser::parse_string_value` emits SSO for strings ≤ 5 bytes (`"perry"` is exactly 5) — so JSON.parse-produced short string values failed every `is_string()` check, fell through to the regular-number branch, and printed as `NaN` because SSO bit patterns ARE NaN doubles. Six coordinated changes: (1) **`crates/perry-runtime/src/builtins.rs`** — new `jsvalue_string_content(value: f64) -> Option<String>` helper at the top of the file centralizes SSO-aware decoding via the existing `crate::string::str_bytes_from_jsvalue`. Replaced `is_string()` arms with `is_any_string()` + helper at five sites: `js_console_log_dynamic` (single-arg `console.log` path), `js_console_error_dynamic` and `js_console_warn_dynamic` (stderr mirrors), `format_jsvalue` (used by `js_console_log_spread` for multi-arg `console.log` and by `console.dir`), `format_jsvalue_for_json` (the JSON-shape pretty-printer). Plus the array-element-quoting check at `format_jsvalue`'s `GC_TYPE_ARRAY` arm widened to `is_any_string()` so SSO array elements still get the `'…'` quotes Node emits. (2) **`js_eq` (the strict `===` runtime called by codegen for unknown-type operands)** — was bit-equality with a number-only special case (line 845-855), so `JSON.parse(...).foo === "perry"` returned false because SSO and heap representations have different bit patterns even when text is identical. Now delegates to `crate::value::js_jsvalue_equals` which has been SSO-aware since v0.5.213 (decodes both sides via `str_bytes_from_jsvalue` and byte-compares). (3) **`js_loose_eq` (the `==` runtime)** — the both-strings branch widened from `is_string() && is_string()` to `is_any_string() && is_any_string()` and routed through `js_jsvalue_equals`; the string-vs-number branches likewise use `is_any_string()` so SSO operands take the same number-coercion path heap strings already had. (4) **`js_string_coerce`** — added an explicit `is_short_string()` arm that calls `crate::string::js_string_materialize_to_heap` to produce a real `*mut StringHeader` for callers that need the heap representation (`String(x)` and other coercion paths). Pre-fix, SSO operands fell through to the regular-number branch and `String(SSO_value)` returned `"NaN"`. (5) **`crates/perry-runtime/src/value.rs::js_get_string_pointer_unified`** — the universal "give me a heap string pointer from any string-like JSValue" helper. Added an SSO arm before the `is_pointer()` check that materializes inline bytes to heap. The 43 codegen sites that call this helper (string equality fast paths, key extraction, etc.) immediately handle SSO correctly without per-site changes; the materialization adds one alloc per call but is the smallest-blast-radius fix and a future codegen pass can switch to `js_jsvalue_equals` to skip the materialize entirely on the equality hot path. (6) **`test-files/test_json_sso_strings.ts`** — new regression test pinning every consumer that was broken: single-arg + multi-arg `console.log` of an SSO value, SSO === heap-string mixed equality (both `===` and `==`), `String()` and `+ ""` coercion, SSO inside a util.inspect-formatted nested object, array of SSO elements via spread, `Object.keys` on an SSO-valued object, JSON.stringify roundtrip — 13 lines all matching Node byte-for-byte. **Verified end-to-end against the issue's exact repro:** `JSON.parse('{"foo":"perry"}').foo` prints `perry` (was `NaN`); `JSON.parse('{"name":"perry"}').name` and `JSON.parse('{"len":"perry"}').len` ditto; `v === "perry"` returns `true` (was `false`); `String(v)` returns `"perry"` (was `"NaN"`). Tests: runtime 168/168, stdlib 33/33, codegen 18/18, hir 20/20, gap 25/28 (unchanged from baseline), all 9 existing `test-files/test_json_*.ts` regression tests still match Node, plus the new `test_json_sso_strings`. Regressions verified: commander v0.5.250, EE/LRU/WSS v0.5.252, Decimal v0.5.259, AsyncLocalStorage v0.5.261, Redis v0.5.270 still all green. **Out of scope** (separate bugs surfaced during investigation): SSO string indexing (`v[0]`, `v.charCodeAt(0)`, etc.) still segfaults — codegen's `IndexGet` and string-method dispatch on Any-typed receivers reads SSO bits as a heap pointer and dereferences arbitrary memory; pre-existing bug, unrelated to the print/equality consumer family fixed here. Mongo `findOne` JSON-string-vs-parsed-object defect from the v0.5.275 follow-up list was the immediate next target this fix unblocks (the deferred defect's repro depended on `JSON.parse(...).foo` working).

## v0.5.278 — Stub audit: `is_inlinable` in `crates/perry-transform/src/inline.rs:213` was inlining functions with rest parameters even though the inliner's `param_map` mechanism only handles 1:1 formal-to-actual arg mapping — so `function format(prefix, ...parts) {...}` called as `format("Items", "a", "b", "c")` got the body inlined with `parts = "a"` (just the first trailing arg, scalar) and the remaining args silently dropped. The body's `parts.length` then read length-of-string `"a"` (1 instead of 3), `parts[0]` indexed as a string char ("h" from "hello"), and `parts.join(",")` interpreted the scalar string as a single array element where `array_join`'s f64-to-string path saw the raw NaN-box bits as a subnormal double (`0.000…0005`). Same bug family as v0.5.273 closure-captures: an inline-pass walker that doesn't know how to handle a particular HIR shape silently does the wrong thing. Fix: bail from `is_inlinable` when any param `is_rest` — symmetric with the existing closures-with-captures and super-call bails. Could be made smarter (synthesize an `Expr::Array(...)` setup_stmt for trailing args), but the conservative fix is safer and the perf cost of skipping inlining for rest-bearing functions is negligible (rest functions are usually variadic helpers, not hot paths). Verified `test_edge_rest_spread_defaults` matches Node byte-for-byte (was diverging on every `parts.join()` / `parts.length` site). Removed from `known_failures.json` (now 17 entries). perry-runtime tests 168/168.

## v0.5.277 — Stub audit: `fs.readFileSync(path)` (no encoding) now returns a real Buffer, matching Node. The codegen at `crates/perry-codegen/src/expr.rs::Expr::FsReadFileBinary` was deliberately calling `js_fs_read_file_sync` (StringHeader, NaN-boxed STRING_TAG) instead of the existing `js_fs_read_file_binary` (BufferHeader, registered in BUFFER_REGISTRY) — a workaround for an old StringHeader-vs-BufferHeader layout-offset bug ("StringHeader is 12 bytes ... BufferHeader is 8 bytes ... causing 'sidebarLocation' to become 'barLocation'"). The workaround stayed past the underlying fix and silently broke `typeof readBack === 'object'` (returned 'string'), `Buffer.isBuffer(readBack)` (returned `false`), and any code reading the result as binary. Fix: route `Expr::FsReadFileBinary` to the binary runtime fn and NaN-box with `nanbox_pointer_inline` (POINTER_TAG); drop the `FsReadFileBinary` branch from the `String` arm in `crates/perry-codegen/src/type_analysis.rs:150` (only `FsReadFileSync` — the explicit-encoding variant — refines to String now). Verified end-to-end: `console.log(buf)` → `<Buffer 68 65 6c 6c 6f>` (was the underlying string), `typeof buf` → `object` (was 'string'), `Buffer.isBuffer(buf)` → `true` (was `false`). `test_cli_simulation` matches Node byte-for-byte (parity-runner's `normalize_output` decodes `<Buffer ...>` lines back to strings, so the CI test was passing pre-fix despite the type-divergence — the fix is for correctness of `typeof` / `isBuffer` checks, not parity output). Removed `test_cli_simulation` from `known_failures.json` (18 entries remaining). perry-runtime tests 168/168.

## v0.5.276 — Bench docs: footnote on `04_array_read`'s 211 MB peak RSS row + new `benchmarks/polyglot/ARRAY_READ_NOTES.md` with analytic working-set math (10M f64 doubling fill, 8M-cap + 16M-cap coexist mid-grow → 192 MB arena peak + ~13 MB overhead), `PERRY_GC_DIAG=1` trace, and `/usr/bin/time -l` confirmation. Confirms the number is legitimate working-set, not a leak.

## v0.5.275 — #187 follow-up: async-factory pattern for `pg`'s `Client`/`Pool` and `mongodb`'s `MongoClient` — the npm-compatible `new T(config); await t.connect()` shape. Also fixes 12 latent NATIVE_MODULE_TABLE row bugs in mongodb (same family as the v0.5.270 ioredis fix). Five coordinated changes: (1) **`crates/perry-stdlib/src/pg/connection.rs`** — `PgConnectionHandle` gains `pending_config: Option<PgConfig>` so the handle can live in two states (pre-connect: config stored, no socket; connected: real PgConnection). New `js_pg_client_new(config: f64) -> Handle` parses config + registers a pre-connect handle. New `js_pg_client_connect(handle) -> Promise<undefined>` snapshots the pending config (taking the value out of the handle to avoid borrowing across the await), opens the connection, stores it. The older combined `js_pg_connect(config) -> Promise<Handle>` is kept wired as the receiver-less `pg.connect(config)` factory pattern. (2) **`crates/perry-stdlib/src/pg/pool.rs`** — `PgPoolHandle` gains `pending_url: Option<String>` (sqlx 0.8's `PgPoolOptions::connect_lazy` panics outside a Tokio runtime context, so the synchronous `new Pool(config)` ctor has nowhere to call it). The actual sqlx pool is now built on first `pool.query()` via a new `ensure_pool()` async helper that runs inside the spawn_for_promise body. New `js_pg_pool_new(config: f64) -> Handle` registers a pre-pool handle; `js_pg_pool_query` calls `ensure_pool` before forwarding to sqlx. (3) **`crates/perry-stdlib/src/mongodb.rs`** — `MongoClientHandle` switches from `client: Client` to `client: Option<Client>` + `pending_uri: Option<String>` mirroring pg. New `js_mongodb_client_new(uri: *StringHeader) -> Handle` (sync) + `js_mongodb_client_connect(handle) -> Promise<undefined>` (parses URI + builds Client async). Also added 9 `_value` wrapper functions (`js_mongodb_collection_insert_one_value`, `_insert_many_value`, `_find_value`, `_find_one_value`, `_update_one_value`, `_update_many_value`, `_delete_one_value`, `_delete_many_value`, `_count_value`) that JSON-stringify their NaN-boxed JSValue arg via `js_json_stringify` before forwarding to the existing JSON-string-taking runtime fns. Pre-fix the dispatch table passed user-supplied JSValue f64 directly into runtime fns signed to receive a `*const StringHeader` — every doc/filter looked like garbage and the user saw `"Invalid document"`. Plus a small `client_ref()` helper that returns a clear "MongoClient not connected — call await client.connect() first" error when the handle is in pre-connect state and a query path tries to use it. (4) **`crates/perry-codegen/src/lower_call.rs::lower_builtin_new`** — three new branches: `"Client"` (calls `js_pg_client_new`), `"Pool"` (calls `js_pg_pool_new`), `"MongoClient"` (calls `js_mongodb_client_new` with `get_raw_string_ptr` for the URI arg). Plus dispatch-row updates: new `module:"pg" has_receiver:true method:"connect" class_filter:Some("Client")` + `class_filter:Some("Pool")` rows for query/end (so Pool routes to `js_pg_pool_query`/`_pool_end` not the Client paths — pre-existing bug since neither was filtered). New `module:"mongodb" has_receiver:true method:"connect"` row for the client.connect() step. Twelve mongodb rows changed from broken stripped names (`js_mongodb_db`, `js_mongodb_insert_one`, `js_mongodb_close`) to the actual runtime symbols (`js_mongodb_client_db`, `js_mongodb_collection_insert_one_value`, `js_mongodb_client_close`, ...) — same shape as the v0.5.270 ioredis row-name fix. The 3 rows for which no runtime exists (`aggregate`, `createIndex`, `toArray`) are commented out so user code calling them falls to the unknown-method sentinel returning `TAG_UNDEFINED` rather than link-failing. (5) **`crates/perry-codegen/src/runtime_decls.rs`** — declared the 5 new pg fns and the 9 new `_value` mongodb wrappers (alphabetized). **Verified end-to-end against a live MongoDB**: `new MongoClient('mongodb://localhost:27017'); await client.connect(); client.db('x').collection('y').insertOne({...}); await client.close()` runs clean (`connected` / `inserted` printed). pg has no live server on this machine but binary links + `new Client({...})` / `new Pool({...})` produce real handles (`typeof === 'object'`) instead of placeholder ObjectHeaders. Tests: stdlib 33/33, runtime 168/168, codegen 18/18, HIR 20/20. Regressions: commander v0.5.250, EE/LRU/WSS v0.5.252, Decimal v0.5.259, AsyncLocalStorage v0.5.261, Redis v0.5.270 — all still green. **Out of scope** (kept around as defects to fix in their own commits): mongo `findOne` resolves the Promise with a JSON STRING, not a parsed object — tried calling `js_json_parse` server-side but a separate Perry-wide JSON-parse-then-property-access bug surfaced (`JSON.parse('{"foo":"perry"}').foo` returns NaN even though `Object.keys` shows `foo` and `typeof a.foo` is `string` — the bit pattern of the STRING_TAG-encoded JSValue prints as NaN at the property-read site). Mongo collection `count` / `delete` runtime fns return raw `u64` instead of `JSValue::number(n).bits()` so user code reads `[object Object]`. WebSocket (client) — uses event-based open notification (`ws.on('open', ...)`) not Promise-resolution-on-connect, so the same sync-ctor + later-connect pattern doesn't apply directly — separate lowering pattern. `Big`/`BigNumber` — still no Rust stdlib. Ship the construction-and-connect win, document the rest.

## v0.5.274 — Bench credibility: add the two comparison rows the page was missing. (1) **simdjson** as a second C++ row alongside nlohmann/json. simdjson is the SIMD-accelerated JSON parser reference (https://simdjson.org); cherry-picking weak C++ libraries was the credibility hole the disclaimers section was meant to prevent, and only listing nlohmann did exactly that. simdjson 4.3.0 from `brew install simdjson`; bench uses `ondemand` for parse + `doc.raw_json()` for stringify (the unmutated-parse fast path, analogous to Perry's lazy tape). New files: `benchmarks/json_polyglot/bench_simdjson.cpp` + `bench_field_access_simdjson.cpp`. **Result: simdjson leads both workloads decisively** — 28 ms validate-and-roundtrip (vs Perry's 89 ms), 25 ms parse-and-iterate (vs Perry's 476 ms). Listed visibly in TL;DR §A and §B as the headline-leading row; Perry's bullet point in the strengths section now honestly says "best in dynamic-typing pack" rather than "leads the field". (2) **AssemblyScript + json-as** as a TS-to-native peer. Tried porffor first (the more direct AOT TS compiler the spec preferred) — porffor 0.61.13 produced incorrect output and segfaulted on the 10k-record workload, alpha-quality, not bench-ready. Static Hermes (`shermes`) not available on Homebrew or npm. Settled on AssemblyScript: TypeScript-like compiles to wasm, run via `wasmtime`. Uses json-as 1.3.2 for compile-time-generated (de)serializers (same approach as Rust serde). New `benchmarks/json_polyglot/as_workspace/` with `assembly/{bench,bench_field_access}.ts` + `asconfig.json` extending `@assemblyscript/wasi-shim`. Caveat: AS is strictly typed, so the workload uses concrete `Item`/`Nested` classes rather than `items: any[]` — closer in shape to the Rust/Kotlin typed-struct rows than the dynamic-typing JS rows; documented explicitly. **Result**: 669 ms validate-and-roundtrip, 660 ms parse-and-iterate — competitive with the typed-struct cohort, slower than Rust serde_json. Both rows appear in TL;DR §A and §B with full per-cell stats. README "JSON libraries used" + flags table + "Honest disclaimers" sections updated to reflect the new comparisons; Perry's strengths bullet recalibrated. Run script auto-detects simdjson (via `brew --prefix simdjson`) and AS (via `as_workspace/node_modules`); both fall through gracefully if missing. Acceptance: ✅ both new rows in both JSON tables, ✅ libraries-used table covers both nlohmann and simdjson with one-line rationale each, ✅ disclaimers section calls out where Perry now loses.

## v0.5.273 — Stub audit: closure-null family fix. The HIR inline pass at `crates/perry-transform/src/inline.rs:1573` walked closure bodies to remap local IDs but did NOT remap the closure's `captures` / `mutable_captures` lists. When a function with an inner closure was inlined (e.g., `function makeAccumulator() { const items = []; return { add: x => items.push(x), ... }; }` called from module init), the inline pass renamed the body's `LocalGet(items)` references to fresh IDs but left `captures: [old_id]` pointing at the now-defunct id. Codegen at `crates/perry-codegen/src/expr.rs::Expr::Closure` then couldn't resolve the capture in the inlined-into FnCtx and fell back to `double_literal(0.0)` per the boxed-cap escape branch — producing null box pointers at runtime, with the symptom being `[PERRY WARN] js_box_get: null box pointer #N` and incorrect output for any closure-capturing-mutable-binding pattern. Fix: extend the `Expr::Closure` arm of `substitute_locals` to call `retain_mut` on both `captures` and `mutable_captures`, remapping each id via `param_map` (LocalGet → new id; trivial-expr inlines → drop now-orphan capture; module-level → unchanged). Verified: `test_closure_capture_types` / `test_edge_closures` / `test_edge_scope_hoisting` all match Node byte-for-byte across two isolated runs each. Removed from `known_failures.json` (now 19 entries down from 22). perry-runtime 168/168, perry-hir 20/20, perry-transform 0/0 — all green.

## v0.5.272 — Bench refactor (code landing): the v0.5.271 entry below described two new benchmarks and a README restructure, but only metadata changes (CLAUDE.md, Cargo.toml) actually shipped under v0.5.271 due to a race during commit. This commit lands the actual benchmark source files, runner updates, and refreshed RESULTS.md / README.md / RESULTS_AUTO.md numbers. New files: `benchmarks/suite/17_loop_data_dependent.ts`, `benchmarks/json_polyglot/bench_field_access.{ts,go,rs,swift,cpp,kt}`. `bench_loop_data_dependent` function added to all 6 polyglot bench.X files (rs/cpp/go/swift/java/py). Both run scripts updated to include the new benches with no special-case invocation; `.gitignore` exception added for `benchmarks/json_polyglot/bench_*.{cpp,go,rs,swift,kt,java}` (the broad `bench_*` rule was hiding the new source files).

## v0.5.271 — Bench refactor: add the two benchmarks that address the most-likely skeptic objections to this README within 30 seconds of reading it. (1) **`loop_data_dependent`** — sibling to `loop_overhead` with a multiplicative carry through `sum` and runtime-loaded array reads (kernel `sum = sum * x[i%64] + x[(i*7)%64]`, x in `[0.5, 1.0)` so the chain contracts to a bounded fixed point). LLVM cannot apply reassoc, IV-simplify, or vectorization — verified at the asm level (rustc 1.85 stable, `cargo rustc --release -- --emit=asm`, loop body LBB5_41 is a 4-instruction scalar fmul/fadd chain with two array loads, comment in `polyglot/bench.rs:122` records the exact dump). Result: Perry / Rust / C++ / Swift / Java / Node / Bun all land within 6 ms of each other (228-233 ms median); Go is the outlier at 132 ms. **The "Perry is 7× faster than C++" headline from `loop_overhead` does NOT replicate when the compiler can't fold** — that's the honest finding this bench was designed to surface. Added to `benchmarks/suite/17_loop_data_dependent.ts` plus `bench_loop_data_dependent` function in all 6 polyglot bench.X files. (2) **`bench_field_access` (JSON parse-and-iterate)** — companion to the existing roundtrip bench that FORCES Perry's lazy tape to materialize. Per iteration: parse → sum every record's nested.x (touches every element) → stringify. Added 6 implementations (`bench_field_access.{ts,go,rs,swift,cpp,kt}`). On this workload **Perry doesn't lead**: median 482 ms (gen-gc + lazy tape) — slower than its own mark-sweep escape-hatch mode at 384 ms (the lazy tape pays overhead it can't amortize when every element gets touched). Rust serde_json wins at 201 ms; Bun is competitive at 260 ms. **README restructure**: `loop_overhead` and the other flag-aggressiveness probes (`math_intensive`, `accumulate`, `array_read`, `array_write`) demoted to a new "Optimization probes (compiler flag-aggressiveness, not runtime perf)" subsection with explicit framing — they measure whether the compiler applied reassoc + IV-simplify + autovectorize, NOT runtime perf. The headline compute table now shows 4 cells: `fibonacci`, `loop_data_dependent`, `object_create`, `nested_loops`. JSON section renamed `JSON parse + stringify` → `JSON validate-and-roundtrip` (TL;DR §A) with new sibling `JSON parse-and-iterate` (TL;DR §B); both stay headline. Both run scripts updated; runner accepts the new benches with no special-case invocation. RUNS=11 fresh data across all benches.

## v0.5.270 — #187 follow-up: `Redis` (ioredis) end-to-end + fixes a pre-existing dispatch-table-symbol-mismatch bug. Three coordinated changes: (1) **`crates/perry-hir/src/ir.rs:46`** — added `"ioredis"` to `NATIVE_MODULES` (replacing the prior `// Note: ioredis NOT in NATIVE_MODULES` comment with one explaining the change). The old workaround (class-name-only tracking in `lower.rs:910` keeping ioredis out of `NATIVE_MODULES`) was needed when `import { Redis } from 'ioredis'` was expected to fall through to a JS interpreter — but Perry's native Rust ioredis impl is the canonical path and the JS fallback path no longer runs anything. Keeping it out of NATIVE_MODULES forced `requires_stdlib("ioredis") → false`, which made `Linking (runtime-only)` skip the stdlib archive — every direct `js_ioredis_*` reference link-failed with `Undefined symbols`. Listing it triggers `database-redis` feature (`stdlib_features.rs:47`) so the linker pulls in the right stdlib subset. (2) **`crates/perry-codegen/src/lower_call.rs::lower_builtin_new`** — new `"Redis"` branch calling `js_ioredis_new(0)` (the runtime fn ignores its config arg and reads connection settings from `REDIS_HOST`/`REDIS_PORT`/`REDIS_PASSWORD`/`REDIS_TLS` env vars; connect is lazy on first method call). Pre-fix `new Redis()` fell into the empty-placeholder branch and every chained method dispatched against junk. (3) **`NATIVE_MODULE_TABLE` ioredis row symbol fix** — pre-existing latent bug: all 9 ioredis dispatch rows referenced runtime symbols `js_redis_*` (without the `io` prefix) but the actual stdlib functions are `js_ioredis_*`. Fixed `createClient` / `set` / `get` / `del` / `exists` / `incr` / `decr` / `expire` / `quit` to point at the real symbols. The bug was dormant because pre-#187 no codepath could reach a real Redis handle — `new Redis()` produced a junk receiver, methods dispatched against it never actually linked the symbol because the link-time reachability analysis stripped them. With the v0.5.264 ctor making the receiver real, the dispatch rows now actually link. The `createClient` row aliases to `js_ioredis_new` (npm `redis`'s `createClient(opts)` and ioredis's `new Redis(opts)` are shape-compatible: both produce a client; opts is host/port/etc., which we read from env vars regardless). **Verified end-to-end against a live Redis (redis-cli ping = PONG):** `await r.set('k', 'hello-perry-' + Date.now())`, `await r.get('k')` returns the value, `await r.del('k')` then `await r.get('k')` returns `null`, `await r.quit()` clean. Tests: stdlib 33/33, runtime 168/168, codegen 18/18, HIR 20/20. Regressions: commander v0.5.250, EE/LRU/WSS v0.5.252, Decimal v0.5.259, AsyncLocalStorage v0.5.261 all still green. **Out of scope (still)**: `Big`/`BigNumber` (no Rust stdlib), `Pool`/`Client` (pg), `MongoClient` (mongodb), `WebSocket` (ws client) — these use async factory functions returning `Promise<T>` (`js_pg_connect`/`js_pg_create_pool`/`js_mongodb_connect`/`js_ws_connect`); `new T()` for those needs Promise-wrapped allocation that's a different lowering pattern entirely.

## v0.5.263 — Stub-audit follow-up: (1) latent type-discrimination bug in `js_promise_all` / `js_promise_race` / `js_promise_any` — same shape as the Promise.allSettled fix landed at `32c997ca` (v0.5.260 era). All three were calling `js_nanbox_get_pointer(promise_f64).is_null()` to detect non-Promise inputs, but STRING_TAG and BIGINT_TAG NaN-boxed values produce non-null lower-48-bit pointers, so they were silently passed to `js_promise_then` as if they were Promises (UB; plain numbers happened to escape because their bit patterns made `js_nanbox_get_pointer` return 0 via the fallback). Fixed all three in `crates/perry-runtime/src/promise.rs:758/884/1156` by reordering the discrimination: check `js_value_is_promise(promise_f64) == 0` (which walks back to the GcHeader's `obj_type`) BEFORE extracting the pointer, mirroring the agent's allSettled fix exactly. Smoke-test with mixed Promise/string/number/bigint inputs: `Promise.all([Promise.resolve(1), "two", 3, Promise.resolve("four")])` returns `[1,"two",3,"four"]`; `Promise.race(["wins", Promise.resolve("loses")])` returns `"wins"`; `Promise.any(["fast", ...])` returns `"fast"`; bigint sibling `Promise.all([Promise.resolve(1n), 2n])` returns `[1n,2n]` — all match Node byte-for-byte. (2) **Re-validated every entry in `test-parity/known_failures.json`** against current behavior. 16 of 33 entries (48%) actually pass today on macOS host. After excluding `ci-env` (still fail on macOS-14 CI runner) and `flake` (intermittent) entries, **11 deterministic-pass entries removed**: `test_edge_class_advanced` / `test_edge_classes` / `test_edge_complex_patterns` / `test_edge_generics` / `test_edge_interfaces` / `test_gap_map_set_extended` / `test_gap_string_methods` / `test_getters_setters` / `test_method_inherit` / `test_perf_paths` / `test_super_calls`. Each verified passing twice in isolation (no flakiness). The `test_gap_map_set_extended` removal is consistent with v0.5.176's -0/+0 fix; the class/inheritance ones likely benefited from the v0.5.249 monomorph property-type-check + the v0.5.245-era cross-module getter/setter fix. Net: known_failures shrank from 33 → **22 entries**, all of which were independently verified to still fail (or be CI-env-only / flake). perry-runtime tests 168/168 unchanged.

## v0.5.262 — Fix #95 (Android half): `notificationRegisterRemote` + `notificationOnReceive` actually wire to FCM on Android. Pre-fix the FFI symbols resolved at link time but the Rust shims were no-op stubs. Six pieces: (1) **gradle**: `id("com.google.gms.google-services") version "4.4.2"` plugin in root + app `build.gradle.kts`; `firebase-bom:33.5.1` + `firebase-messaging-ktx` deps. (2) **placeholder `app/google-services.json`**: dummy api_key + project_number so the gradle plugin's parse-and-validate at apply time succeeds — package_name matches the actual `applicationId = "com.skelpo.pickcolor"` (the plugin matches against applicationId not namespace; first attempt with `com.perry.app` failed `:app:processDebugGoogleServices`). User overlays this file with their real Firebase project's `google-services.json` to make FCM actually authenticate; the placeholder lets the build succeed but the SDK rejects it at runtime. (3) **`PerryFirebaseMessagingService.kt`** extends `FirebaseMessagingService`. `onNewToken` forwards the token string to native via `PerryBridge.nativeNotificationToken`; `onMessageReceived` serializes the `RemoteMessage` to JSON via `org.json.JSONObject` (data map + notification block fields: title/body/tag/color/icon/sound/clickAction/channelId, plus from/messageId/messageType/sentTime/ttl) and forwards via `PerryBridge.nativeNotificationReceive`. `UnsatisfiedLinkError` caught for the cold-start broadcast case (#98 territory). (4) **`AndroidManifest`**: `<service android:name=".PerryFirebaseMessagingService" android:exported="false">` with intent-filter for `com.google.firebase.MESSAGING_EVENT`. (5) **`PerryBridge.registerForRemoteNotifications(activity)`**: calls `FirebaseMessaging.getInstance().token.addOnSuccessListener { nativeNotificationToken(it) }`. The outer `try { … } catch (Throwable)` wraps the FCM init to handle the placeholder-google-services.json case — logs + continues without crashing. Two new externs: `nativeNotificationToken(token: String)` + `nativeNotificationReceive(payloadJson: String)`. (6) **Rust** (`crates/perry-ui-android/src/system.rs`): two new statics `NOTIFICATION_REMOTE_TOKEN_KEY` + `NOTIFICATION_RECEIVE_KEY`. `notification_register_remote(callback)` registers via the existing `crate::callback::register` global table, saves the key, and calls `PerryBridge.registerForRemoteNotifications` via JNI to kick off the initial token fetch. `notification_on_receive(callback)` just stores the callback. New JNI exports `Java_com_perry_app_PerryBridge_nativeNotificationToken` (token → NaN-boxed string → `invoke1`) and `_nativeNotificationReceive` (JSON string → `js_json_parse` to a Perry object → `invoke1`). The two `lib.rs` FFI shims that were `_unused` no-op stubs now route through. **Caveats** (in addition to the placeholder-json one): no `WAKE_LOCK` permission added — FCM SDK requests it transitively but heavy-message-volume apps may want the explicit declaration; no notification-icon metadata (`com.google.firebase.messaging.default_notification_icon` etc.) set so server-side notification-shape pushes use the system default; cold-start broadcast (process killed but FCM payload arrives) still drops messages — that's #98 territory and would need to refactor the JNI dispatcher to lazily init the Perry runtime before invoking the callback. Background delivery beyond what `FirebaseMessagingService.onMessageReceived` natively gives us isn't wired. Verified: `cargo check -p perry-ui-android` clean; `./gradlew :app:processDebugGoogleServices` → BUILD SUCCESSFUL (placeholder validates); `./gradlew :app:compileDebugKotlin` → BUILD SUCCESSFUL with the firebase-messaging-ktx dep linked. End-to-end runtime validation needs the user's real Firebase project + `google-services.json` overlay + a real Android device + an APNs-equivalent push from the Firebase console.

## v0.5.261 — #187 follow-up: `AsyncLocalStorage` (async_hooks) end-to-end. Same `new T()` placeholder bug as #187 / Decimal / EE/LRU/WSS — `Expr::New { class_name: "AsyncLocalStorage" }` fell into `lower_call.rs:1855`'s empty `js_object_alloc(0,0)` branch, and **on top of that** the 5 instance methods (`run`/`getStore`/`enterWith`/`exit`/`disable`) had **zero** rows in `NATIVE_MODULE_TABLE` so even with a real handle, every call dispatched against the unknown-method sentinel returning `0.0` / `TAG_UNDEFINED`. Pre-fix `als.run('x', () => console.log(als.getStore()))` printed nothing — the callback never fired and the store was never recorded. Two coordinated changes: (1) **`crates/perry-codegen/src/lower_call.rs`** — new `"AsyncLocalStorage"` branch in `lower_builtin_new` calling `js_async_local_storage_new()` and NaN-boxing as POINTER. 5 new `NATIVE_MODULE_TABLE` rows for `module: "async_hooks"`: `run` (NA_F64 store + NA_PTR closure → `_run`), `getStore` (no args → `_get_store`), `enterWith` (NA_F64 store → `_enter_with`, NR_VOID), `exit` (NA_PTR closure → `_exit`), `disable` (no args → `_disable`, NR_VOID). The runtime functions in `crates/perry-stdlib/src/async_local_storage.rs` were already complete + already declared in `runtime_decls.rs:1120-1125` from prior work — just had no callers. The `_run` and `_exit` runtime fns take the closure pointer as raw `i64` (NA_PTR coerces from NaN-boxed value) and call `js_closure_call0` internally with `nullptr` checks. (2) Verified end-to-end against Node 25.8 (`--experimental-strip-types`): all 10 lines of a comprehensive test (basic run + outside-run undefined + nested A→B + enterWith persistence + disable clears + exit-temporarily-clears semantic) match byte-for-byte. Tests: regression sweep clean — commander v0.5.250, EE/LRU v0.5.252, Decimal v0.5.259 all still green. **GC caveat**: stored `f64` JS values held in the per-handle `stores: Vec<f64>` are not yet anchored by a registered root scanner — during a `run(...)` invocation the store is also on the Rust call stack so conservative scanning catches it, but a long-lived `enterWith(obj)` followed by a malloc-triggered GC could in principle sweep the object. No reproducer hit yet; matching `events.rs`'s `for_each_handle_of` scanner pattern would close this — deferred as polish. **Out of scope (still)**: `Big`/`BigNumber` (no Rust stdlib), `Redis` (excluded from `NATIVE_MODULES`), `Pool`/`Client`/`MongoClient`/`WebSocket(client)` (need Promise-wrapped allocation pattern).

## v0.5.260 — Fix #96 (Android half): `notificationSchedule` (interval + calendar) and `notificationCancel` actually fire on Android. Pre-fix `perry_system_notification_schedule_*` and `_cancel` in `crates/perry-ui-android/src/lib.rs` were no-op stubs; the FFI symbols resolved at link time but the work was discarded silently. Five coordinated pieces: (1) **Kotlin BroadcastReceiver**: new `PerryScheduledNotificationReceiver.kt` listens on action `com.perry.app.SCHEDULED_FIRE`. When `AlarmManager` fires, it builds + posts the notification with the same channel + tap-routing as `sendNotification` — extracts `id`/`title`/`body` from intent extras, lazy-creates `"perry-default"` channel, gates on POST_NOTIFICATIONS at API 33+, attaches a tap PendingIntent targeting `PerryNotificationReceiver` (#97) so taps on scheduled notifications still fire the JS callback. (2) **AndroidManifest** registers the receiver with `exported="false"`. (3) **`PerryBridge.kt` schedule + cancel methods**: `scheduleInterval(activity, id, title, body, seconds, repeats)` calls `AlarmManager.setRepeating(RTC_WAKEUP, …)` for `repeats=true` (caps interval at 60s minimum since Android coalesces shorter intervals) or `setAndAllowWhileIdle` for one-shots — inexact but Doze-safe and **permission-free**, unlike `setExact*` which needs `SCHEDULE_EXACT_ALARM` on API 31+. `scheduleCalendar(activity, id, title, body, timestampMs)` uses `setAndAllowWhileIdle(RTC_WAKEUP, timestampMs.toLong(), pi)`. `cancelNotification(activity, id)` looks up the existing PendingIntent via `FLAG_NO_CREATE` (returns `null` if the alarm was never scheduled or was already fired) and calls `AlarmManager.cancel(pi)` + `pi.cancel()` to tear the registration down, plus `NotificationManagerCompat.from(activity).cancel(id.hashCode())` to dismiss any already-displayed notification. PendingIntent request code = `id.hashCode()` so the same string id consistently maps to the same PendingIntent slot across schedule + cancel. New `buildScheduledPendingIntent` helper centralizes the PendingIntent + extras shape so the schedule fns share one code path. (4) **`sendNotification` refactor**: the `notify` int id and PendingIntent request code now both derive from `"perry_notification".hashCode()` (new `PERRY_DEFAULT_ID` const) instead of the stale `PERRY_DEFAULT_NOTIFICATION_ID = 1` — so `cancelNotification("perry_notification")` actually cancels a `notificationSend`-posted notification, matching iOS where `requestWithIdentifier:"perry_notification"` is the same canonical id across send + cancel. (5) **Rust JNI dispatchers**: `crates/perry-ui-android/src/system.rs` gains `notification_schedule_interval` / `_calendar` / `_location` / `_cancel` functions that `JNIEnv.call_static_method` into the new Kotlin methods with the right type signatures (interval = `(Activity, String, String, String, double, boolean)V`, calendar = `(Activity, String, String, String, double)V`, cancel = `(Activity, String)V`). `repeats` arrives as a JS-truthy NaN-boxed f64 and gets coerced via `js_is_truthy` before crossing the JNI boundary as a real `boolean`. The four `lib.rs` FFI shims that were `_unused` no-op stubs now actually call into `system::*`. **`schedule_location` stays a logged no-op** (`__android_log_print` warning) — Geofencing API needs `FUSED_LOCATION_PROVIDER` from Google Play Services + a runtime `ACCESS_FINE_LOCATION` grant, which is a separate scope expansion not worth bundling here. **Caveats**: alarms are inexact — `scheduleInterval(N)` may fire up to a few minutes late on a Doze-throttled device; `scheduleCalendar(date)` likewise. Apps needing exact wall-clock fire have to request `SCHEDULE_EXACT_ALARM` themselves and switch to `setExactAndAllowWhileIdle`. Cross-process kills also lose the alarm registration (the OS persists alarms across the receiver's process death but reboots wipe them — a `BOOT_COMPLETED` receiver to re-arm them after reboot is a separate piece). Verified: `cargo check -p perry-ui-android` clean, `./gradlew :app:compileDebugKotlin` → BUILD SUCCESSFUL. End-to-end runtime validation needs a real Android device + scheduled notification + waiting for the alarm to fire. **Out of scope**: Android #95 (Firebase Messaging), `scheduleLocation` (Geofencing), exact-alarm permission flow.
